be no incongruity in the idea that in the very earliest period of man 's habitation of this world he make a friend and companion of some sort of aboriginal representative of we modern dog and that in return for its aid in protect he from wilder animal and in guard he sheep and goat he give it a share of he food a corner in he dwelling and grow to trust it and care for it probably the animal be originally little else than a unusually gentle jackal or a ail wolf drive by its companion from the wild maraud pack to seek shelter in alien surroundings one can well conceive the possibility of the partnership beginning in the circumstance of some helpless whelp be bring home by the early hunter to be tend and rear by the woman and child the present-day savage of new guinea and mid-africa do not as a rule take the trouble to tame and train a adult wild animal for he own purpose and primitive man be surely equally indifferent to the questionable advantage of harbour a dangerous guest but a litter of woolly whelp introduce into the home as plaything for the child would grow to regard themselves and be regard as member of the family and it would soon be find that the hunting instinct of the mature animal be of value to he captor the savage master tread the primeval forest in search of food would not fail to recognize the helpfulness of a keener nose and sharper eye even than he own unsullied sens while the dog in he turn would find a better shelter in association with man than if he be hunting on he own account thus mutual benefit would result in some kind of tacit agreement of partnership and through the generation the wild wolf or jackal would gradually become gentler more docile and tractable and the dreaded enemy of the flock develop into the trust guardian of the fold in nearly all part of the world trace of a indigenous dog family be find the only exception be the west indian island madagascar the eastern island of the malayan archipelago new zealand and the polynesian island where there be no sign that any dog wolf or fox have exist as a true aboriginal animal in the ancient oriental land and generally among the early mongolian the dog remain savage and neglect for century prowl in pack gaunt and wolf-like as it prowl to-day through the street and under the wall of every eastern city no attempt be make to allure it into human companionship or to improve it into docility it be not until we come to examine the record of the higher civilisation of assyrium and egypt that we discover any distinct variety of canine form assyrian sculpture depict two such a greyhound and a mastiff the latter describe in the tablet as the chained-up mouth-opening dog that be to say it be use as a watch-dog and several variety be refer to in the cuneiform inscription preserve in the british museum the egyptian monument of about 3000 bc present many form of the domestic dog and there can be no doubt that among the ancient egyptian it be as completely a companion of man as much a favorite in the house and a help in the chase as it be among ourselves at present in the city of cynopolis it be reverence next to the sacred jackal and on the death of a dog the member of the household to which he have belong carefully shave they whole body and religiously abstain from use the food of whatever kind which happen to be in the house at the time among the distinct breed keep in egypt there be a massive wolf-dog a large heavily-built hound with drooping ear and a pointed head at least two variety of greyhound use for hunting the gazelle and a small breed of terrier or turnspit with short crooked leg this last appear to have be regard as a especial household pet for it be admit into the living room and take as a companion for walk out of door it be furnish with a collar of leaf or of leather or precious metal work into the form of leaf and when it die it be embalmed every town throughout egypt have its place of interment for canine mummy the dog be not greatly appreciate in palestine and in both the old and new testament it be commonly speak of with scorn and contempt as a unclean beast even the familiar reference to the sheepdog in the book of job -- _ but now they that be younger than i have I in derision whose father i would have disdain to set with the dog of my flock _ -- be not without a suggestion of contempt and it be roman as also by the ancient barbaric tribe of the western hemisphere the important question now arise : have all these dog a common origin in a definite parent stock or do they spring from separate and unrelated parent half a century ago it be believe that all the evidence which could be bring to bear upon the problem point to a independent origin of the dog youatt write in 1845 argue that this power of trace back the dog to the very earliest period of history and the fact that he then seem to be as sagacious as faithful and as valuable as at the present day strongly favor the opinion that he be descend from no inferior and comparatively worthless animal and that he be not the progeny of the wolf the jackal or the fox but be originally create somewhat as we now find he the associate and entirely dismiss the theory of relationship one thing be certain that fox do not breed in confinement except in very rare instance the silver fox of north america be the only species record to have the trail of the quarry the other endeavor to intercept its retreat exercise a considerable amount of strategy a trait which be exhibit by many of we sport dog and terrier when hunting in team a when he be not familiarly know it be possible that the mastiff owe he origin to some remote ancestor of alien strain the assyrian king possess a large dog of decide mastiff type and use it in the to see another old and valuable strain be keep by the duke of devonshire at chatsworth it be to these two strain that the dog of the present day trace back mr woolmore 's crown prince be one of the for the fault in many specimen of more recent year unfortunately he be indiscriminately breed from with the result that in a very short time breeder find it impossible to find a mastiff unrelated to he it be to be deplore that ever since he era there have be a perceptible diminution in the number of good example of this fine old english breed and that from be a admire and fashionable dog the take from the old english mastiff club 's _ point of a mastiff _ be admirable as a standard to which future breeder should aim to attain \* \* \* \* \* point of the mastiff : general character and symmetry -- large massive powerful symmetrical and well-knit frame a combination of grandeur and good nature courage and docility general description of head -- in general outline give a square appearance when view from any point breadth greatly to be desire and should be in ratio to length of the whole head and face as 2 to 3 general description of body -- massive broad deep long powerfully build on leg wide apart and squarely set muscle sharply define size a great desideratum if combine with quality height and substance important if both point be proportionately combine skull -- broad between the ear forehead flat but wrinkle when attention be excite brow -lrb- superciliary ridge -rrb- slightly raise muscle of the temple and cheek -lrb- temporal and masseter -rrb- well develop arch across the skull of a round flatten curve with a depression up the center of the forehead from the medium line between the eye to half way up the sagittal suture face or muzzle -- short broad under the eye and keep nearly parallel in width to the end of the nose truncate _ ie _ blunt and cut off square thus form a right angle with the upper line of the face of great depth from the point of the nose to under jaw under jaw broad to the end canine tooth healthy powerful and wide apart incisor level or the lower project beyond the upper but never sufficiently so as to become visible when the mouth be close nose broad with widely spread nostril when view from the front flat -lrb- not pointed or turn up -rrb- in profile lip diverge at obtuse angle with the septum and slightly pendulous so as to show a square profile length of muzzle to whole head and face as 1 to 3 circumference of muzzle -lrb- measure midway between the eye and nose -rrb- to that of the head -lrb- measure before the ear -rrb- as 3 to 5 ear -- small thin to the touch wide apart set on at the highest point of the side of the skull so as to continue the outline across the summit and lie flat and close to the cheek when in repose eye -- small wide apart divide by at least the space of two eye the stop between the eye well marked but not too abrupt color hazel-brown the darker the better showing no haw neck chest and rib -- neck -- slightly arched moderately long very muscular and measure in circumference about one or two inch less than the skull before the ear chest -- wide deep and well let down between the fore-leg rib arch and well-rounded false rib deep and well set back to the hip girth should be one-third more than the height at the shoulder shoulder and arm -- slightly slope heavy and muscular fore-leg and foot -- leg straight strong and set wide apart bone very large elbow square pastern upright foot large and round toe well arch up nail black back loin and flank -- back and loin wide and muscular flat and very wide in a bitch slightly arch in a dog great depth of flank hind-leg and foot -- hind-quarter broad wide and muscular with well develop second thigh hock bent wide apart and quite squarely set when stand or walk foot round tail -- put on high up and reach to the hock or a little below they wide at its root and taper to the end hang straight in repose but form a curve with the end point upward but not over the back when the dog be excite coat -- color -- coat short and close lie but not too fine over the shoulder neck and back color apricot or silver fawn or dark fawn-brindle in any case muzzle ear and nose should be black with black round the orbit and extend upward between they \* \* \* \* \* size be a quality very desirable in this breed the height of many dog of olden day be from thirty-two to thirty-three inch the height should be obtain rather from great depth of body than length of leg a leggy mastiff be very undesirable thirty inch may be take as a fair average height for dog and bitch somewhat less many of mr lukey 's stand 32 inch and over mr green 's monarch be over 33 inch the shah 32 inch and cardinal 32 inch the method of rear a mastiff have much to do with its ultimate size but it be perhaps needless to say that the selection of the breed stock have still more to do with this it be therefore essential to select a dog and bitch of a large strain to obtain large mastiff it be not so necessary that the dog themselves should be so large as that they come from a large strain the weight of a full-grown dog should be anything over 160 lb many have turn over the scale at 180 lb the shah for instance be 182 lb in weight scawfell over 200 lb one of the great difficulty that breeder of mastiff and all other large dog have to contend against be in rear the puppy so many bitch be clumsy and apt to kill the whelp by lie on they it be therefore always better to be provide with one or more foster bitch at about six week old a fairly good opinion may be form as to what the puppy will ultimately turn out in certain respects for although they may change materially during growth the good or bad quality which be manifest at that early age will in all probability be apparent when the puppy have reach maturity it be therefore frequently easier to select the best puppy in the nest than to do so when they be from six to nine or ten month old puppy should be allow all the liberty possible and never be tie up : they should be take out for steady gentle exercise and not permit to get too fat or they become too heavy with detrimental result to they leg many mastiff puppy be very shy and nervous but they will grow out of this if kindly handle and eventually become the best guard and protector it be possible to have the temper of a mastiff should be take into consideration by the breeder they be as a rule possess of the best of temper a savage dog with such power as the mastiff possess be indeed a dangerous creature and therefore some inquiry as to the temper of a stud dog should be make before decide to use he in these dog as in all other it be a question of how they be treat by the person have charge of they the feeding of puppy be a important matter and should be carefully see to by anyone wish to rear they successfully if goat 's milk be procurable it be preferable to cow 's milk the price ask for it be sometimes prohibitory but this difficulty may be surmount in many case by keep a goat or two on the premise many breeder have obtain a goat with the sole object of rear a litter of puppy on she milk and have eventually discard cow 's milk altogether use goat 's milk for household purpose instead as soon as the puppy will lap they should be induce to take arrowroot prepare with milk oatmeal and maizemeal about one quarter of the latter to three quarter of the former make a good food for puppy dog biscuit and the various hound meal soak in good broth may be use with advantage but no dog either large or small can be keep in condition for any length of time without a fair proportion of meat of some kind sheep 's paunch clean and well boil mixed with sweet stale bread previously soak in cold water make a excellent food and can hardly be excel as a staple diet in feed on horseflesh care should be take to ascertain that the horse be not diseased especially if any be give uncooked worm be a constant source of trouble from the earliest day of puppy-hood and no puppy suffering from they will thrive every effort therefore should be make to get rid of they with proper feeding groom exercise and cleanliness any large dog can be keep in good condition without resort to medicine the use of which should be strictly prohibit unless there be real need for it mastiff keep under such condition be far more likely to prove successful stud dog and brood bitch than those to which deleterious drug be constantly be give chapter iii the bulldog the bulldog be know to have be domicile in this country for several century like the mastiff of which it be a smaller form it be a descendant of the alaunt mastive or bandog describe by dr caius who state that the mastyve or bandogge be vaste huge stubborne ougly and eager of a hevy and burthenous body and therefore but of little swiftnesse terrible and frightful to beholde and more fearce and fall than any arcadian curre the first mention of bulldog as the distinctive name of this now national breed occur in a letter write by prestwich eaton from st sebastian to george wellingham in st swithin 's lane london in 1631 or 1632 for a good mastive dogge a case of bottle replenish with the best lickor and pray proceur mee two good bulldogg and let they be send by ye first shipp obviously the name be derive from the dog 's association with the sport of bull-bait the object aim at in that pursuit be that the dog should pin and hold the bull by the muzzle and not leave it the bull be naturally helpless when seize in he most tender part as he lower he head in order to use he horn it be necessary for the dog to keep close to the ground or in the word of the old fancier of the sport to play low larger dog be at a disadvantage in this respect and therefore those of smaller proportion which be quite as suitable for the sport be select the average height of the dog be about 16 inch and the weight be generally about 45 lb whilst the body be broad muscular and compact as be show in scott 's well-known engraving of crib and rosa when bull-baiting be prohibit by law the sportsman of the period turn they attention to dog-fighting and for this pastime the bulldog be specially train the chief centre in london where these exhibition take place be the westminster pit the bear garden at bankside and the old conduit field in bayswater in order to obtain greater quickness of movement many of the bulldog be cross with a terrier although some fancier rely on the pure breed it be record that lord camelford 's bulldog belcher fight one hundred and four battle without once suffer defeat the decline of bull-baiting and dog-fighting after the passing of the bill prohibit these sport be responsible for a lack of interest in perpetuate the breed of bulldog even in 1824 it be say to be degenerate and gentleman who have previously be the chief breeder gradually desert the fancy at one time it be state that wasp child and billy who be of the duke of hamilton 's strain be the only remain bulldog in existence and that upon they decease the bulldog would become extinct -- a prophecy which all bulldog lover happily find incorrect the specimen alive in 1817 as see in print of that period be not so cloddy as those meet with at the present day still the outline of rosa in the engraving of crib and rosa be consider to represent perfection in the shape make and size of the ideal type of bulldog the only objection which have be take be that the bitch be deficient in wrinkle about the head and neck and in substance of bone in the limb the commencement of the dog-show era in 1859 enable class to be provide for bulldog and a fresh incentive to breed they be offer to the dog fancier in certain district of the country notably in london birmingham sheffield manchester and dudley a number of fancier reside and it be to they effort that we be indebted for the varied specimen of the breed that be to be see at the present time in form a judgment of a bulldog the general appearance be of most importance as the various point of the dog should be symmetrical and well balanced no one point be in excess of the other so as to destroy the impression of determination strength and activity which be convey by the typical specimen he body should be thickset rather low in stature but broad powerful and compact the head should be strikingly massive and large in proportion to the dog 's size it can not be too large so long as it be square that be it must not be wider than it be deep the larger the head in circumference cause by the prominent cheek the greater the quantity of muscle to hold the jaw together the head should be of great depth from the occiput to the base of the lower jaw and should not in any way be wedge-shaped dome-shaped or peaked in circumference the skull should measure in front of the ear at least the height of the dog at the shoulder the cheek should be well rounded extend sideways beyond the eye and be well furnished with muscle length of skull -- that be the distance between the eye and the ear -- be very desirable the forehead should be flat and the skin upon it and about the head very loose hanging in large wrinkle the temple or frontal bone should be very prominent broad square and high cause a wide and deep groove know as the stop between the eye and should extend up the middle of the forehead divide the head vertically be traceable at the top of the skull the expression well break up be use where this stop and furrow be well marked and if there be the attendant looseness of skin the animal 's expression be well finish the face when measure from the front of the cheek-bone to the nose should be short and its skin should be deeply and closely wrinkled excessive shortness of face be not natural and can only be obtain by the sacrifice of the chop such shortness of face make the dog appear smaller in head and less formidable than he otherwise would be formerly this shortness of face be artificially obtain by the use of the jack a atrocious form of torture by which a iron instrument be use to force back the face by means of thumbscrew the nose should be rough large broad and black and this color should extend to the lower lip its top should be deeply set back almost between the eye the distance from the inner corner of the eye to the extreme tip of the nose should not be greater than the length from the tip of the nose to the edge of the under lip the nostril should be large and wide with a well-defined straight line visible between they the largeness of nostril which be a very desirable property be possess by few of the recent prize-winner when view in profile the tip of the nose should touch a imaginary line draw from the extremity of the lower jaw to the top of the center of the skull this angle of the nose and face be know as the lay-back and can only properly be ascertain by view the dog from the side the inclination backward of the nose allow a free passage of the air into the nostril whilst the dog be hold he quarry it be apparent that if the mouth do not project beyond the nose the nostril would be flat against the part to which the dog be fix and breathing would then be stop the upper lip call the chop or flew should be thick broad pendant and very deep hanging completely over the lower jaw at the side but only just join the under lip in front yet cover the tooth completely the amount of cushion which a dog may have be dependent upon the thickness of the flew the lip should not be pendulous the upper jaw should be broad massive and square the tusk be wide apart whilst the lower jaw be turn upward should project in front of the upper the tooth should be large and strong and the six small tooth between the tusk should be in a even row the upper jaw can not be too broad between the tusk if the upper and lower jaw be level and the muzzle be not turn upward the dog be say to be down-faced whilst if the underjaw be not undershoot he be say to be froggy a wry-faced dog be one have the lower jaw twist and this deformity so detract from the general appearance of the dog as seriously to handicap he in the show-ring the underjaw project beyond the upper in order to allow the dog when run directly to the front to grasp the bull and when fix to give he a firmer hold the eye see from the front should be situate low down in the skull as far from the ear the nose and each other as possible but quite in front of the forehead so long as they corner be in a straight line at right angle with the stop and in front of the forehead they should be a little above the level of the base of the nasal bone and should be quite round in shape of moderate size neither sunken nor prominent and be as black in color as possible -- almost if not quite black show no white when look directly to the front a good deal of a bulldog 's appearance depend on the quality shape and carriage of he ear they should be small and thin and set high on the head that be the front inner edge of each ear should as view from the front join the outline of the skull at the top corner of such outline so as to place they as wide apart as high and as far from the eye as possible the shape should be that which be know as rose in which the ear fold inward at the back the upper or front edge curving over outwards and backwards show part of the inside of the burr if the ear be place low on the skull they give a applehead appearance to the dog if the ear fall in front hide the interior as be the case with a fox-terrier it be say to button and this type be highly objectionable unfortunately within the last few year the button and semi-tulip ear have be rather prevalent amongst the specimen on the show bench if the ear be carry erect it be know as a tulip ear and this form also be objectionable nevertheless at the beginning of the nineteenth century two out of every three dog possess ear of this description the neck should be moderate in length very thick deep muscular and short but of sufficient length to allow it to be well arched at the back commence at the junction with the skull there should be plenty of loose thick and wrinkled skin about the throat form a dewlap on each side from the lower jaw to the chest the chest should be very wide laterally round prominent and deep make the dog appear very broad and short-legged in front the shoulder should be broad the blade slope considerably from the body they should be deep very powerful and muscular and should be flat at the top and play loosely from the chest the brisket should be capacious round and very deep from the shoulder to the lowest part where it join the chest and be well let down between the fore-leg it should be large in diameter and round behind the fore-leg neither flat-sided nor sinking which it will not do provide that the first and succeed rib be well round the belly should be well tuck up and not pendulous a small narrow waist be greatly admire the desire object in body formation be to obtain great girth at the brisket and the smallest possible around the waist that be the loin should be arched very high when the dog be say to have a good cut-up the back should be short and strong very broad at the shoulder and comparatively narrow at the loin the back should rise behind the shoulder in a graceful curve to the loin the top of which should be higher than the top of the shoulder thence curve again more suddenly to the tail form a arch know as the roach back which be essentially a characteristic of the breed though unfortunately many lead prize-winner of the present day be entirely deficient in this respect some dog dip very considerably some distance behind the shoulder before the upward curve of the spine begin and these be know as swamp-backed other rise in a almost straight line to the root of the tail and be know as stern-high the tail should be set on low jut out rather straight then turn downward the end point horizontally it should be quite round in its whole length smooth and devoid of fringe or coarse hair it should be moderate in length rather short than long thick at the root and taper quickly to a fine point it should have a downward carriage and the dog should not be able to raise it above the level of the backbone the tail should not curve at the end otherwise it be know as ring-tailed the ideal length of tail be about six inch many fancier demand a screw or kinked tail that be one have congenital dislocation at the joint but such appendage be not desirable in the best interest of the breed the fore-leg should be very stout and strong set wide apart thick muscular and short with well-developed muscle in the calf present a rather bow outline but the bone of the leg must be straight large and not bandy or curved they should be rather short in proportion to the hind-leg but not so short as to make the back appear long or detract from the dog 's activity and so cripple he the elbow should be low and stand well away from the rib so as to permit the body to swing between they if this property be absent the dog be say to be on the leg the ankle or pastern should be short straight and strong the fore-foot should be straight and turn very slightly outwards they should be of medium size and moderately round not too long or narrow whilst the toe should be thick compact and well split up make the knuckle prominent and high the hind-leg though of slighter build than the fore-leg should be strong and muscular they should be longer in proportion than the fore-leg in order to elevate the loin the stifle should be round and turn slightly outwards away from the body thus bend the hock inward and the hind-feet outward the hock should be well let down so that the leg be long and muscular from the loin to the point of the hock which make the pastern short but these should not be so short as those of the fore-leg the hind-feet whilst be smaller than the forefoot should be round and compact with the toe well split up and the knuckle prominent the most desirable weight for a bulldog be about 50 lb the coat should be fine in texture short close and smooth silky when stroke from the head towards the tail owe to its closeness but not wiry when stroke in the reverse direction the color should be whole or smut the latter be a whole color with a black mask or muzzle it should be brilliant and pure of its sort the color in order of merit be first whole color and smut viz brindle red white with they variety as whole fawn fallow etc and secondly pie and mixed color opinion differ considerably on the color question one judge will set back a fawn and put forward a pied dog whilst other will do the reverse occasionally one come across specimen have a black-and-tan color which although not mention in the recognize standard as be debar do not as a rule figure in the prize list some of the best specimen which the writer have see have be black-and-tans and a few year ago on the award of a first prize to a bitch of this color a long but non-conclusive argument be hold in the canine press grant that the color be objectionable a dog which score in all other property should not be put down for this point alone see that in the dog-fighting day there be many specimen of this color in action the bulldog should have a peculiarly heavy and constrain gait a rolling or slouch movement appear to walk with short quick step on the tip of he toe he hind-foot not be lift high but appear to skim the ground and run with the right shoulder rather advance similar to the manner of a horse when canter the foregoing minute description of the various show point of a bulldog indicate that he should have the appearance of a thick-set ayrshire or highland bull in stature he should be low to the ground broad and compact the body be carry between and not on the fore-leg he should stand over a great deal of ground and have the appearance of immense power the height of the fore-leg should not exceed the distance from the elbow to the center of the back between the shoulder blade considerable importance be attach to the freedom and activity display by the animal in its movement deform joint or weakness be very objectionable the head should be strikingly massive and carry low the face short the muzzle very broad blunt and inclined upward the body should be short and well-knit the limb stout and muscular the hind-quarter should be very high and strong but rather lightly make in comparison with the heavily-made fore-part it must be acknowledge that there be many strain of this breed which be constitutionally unsound for this reason it be important that the novice should give very careful consideration to he first purchase of a bulldog he should ascertain beyond all doubt not only that he propose purchase be itself sound in wind and limb but that its sire and dam be and have be in similarly healthy condition the dog to be choose should be physically strong and show pronounced muscular development if these requirement be present and the dog be in no sense a contradiction of the good quality of its progenitor but a justification of its pedigree care and good treatment will do the rest it be to be remembered however that a bulldog may be improve by judicious exercise when at exercise or take a walk with he owner the young dog should always be hold by a leash he will invariably pull vigorously against this restraint but such action be beneficial as it tend to develop the muscle of the shoulder and front of the body when take up the bulldog fancy nine out of every ten novice choose to purchase a male the contrary course should be adopt the female be a equally good companion in the house or on the road she be not less affectionate and faithful and when the inevitable desire to attempt to reproduce the species be reach the beginner have the means at once available it be always difficult for the uninitiated to select what be likely to be a good dog from the nest in choose a puppy care should be take to ensure it have plenty of bone in its limb and these should be fairly short and wide the nostril should be large and the face as short as possible the chop should be thick and heavily wrinkled and the mouth square there should be a distinct indent in the upper jaw where the bone will eventually curve whilst the lower jaw should show sign of curvature and protrude slightly in front of the upper jaw the tooth from canine to canine include the six front tooth should be in a straight line see that the ear be very small and thin and the eye set well apart the puppy have these property together with a domed peaked or cocoanut shaped skull be the one which in nine case out of ten will eventually make the best head dog of the litter the breeding of bulldog require unlimited patience as success be very difficult to attain the breeder who can rear five out of every ten puppy bear may be consider fortunate it be frequently find in what appear to be a healthy lot of puppy that some of they begin to whine and whimper towards the end of the first day and in such case the writer 's experience be that there will be a speedy burial it may be that the cause be due to some acidity of the milk but in such a case one would expect that similar difficulty would be experience with the remainder of the litter but this be not the usual result provide that the puppy can be keep alive until the fourth day it may be take that the chance be well in favor of ultimate success -lrb- illustration : mr and mr arthur mayor 's bulldog ch silent duchess -rrb- many breeder object to feed the mother with meat at this time but the writer once have two litter sister who whelp on the same day and he decide to try the effect of a meat _ versus _ farinaceous diet upon they as a result the bitch who be freely feed with raw beef rear a stronger lot of puppy show better develop bone than do the one who be feed on milk and cereal similarly in order that the puppy after wean may develop plenty of bone and muscle it be advisable to feed once a day upon finely mince raw meat there be some successful breeder indeed who invariably give to each puppy a teaspoonful of cod liver oil in the morning and a similar dose of extract of malt in the evening with the result that there be never any rickety or weak dog in the kennel whilst the development of the bone in the skull and limb be most pronounced owe to they lethargic disposition young bulldog be somewhat liable to indigestion and during the period of puppyhood it be of advantage to give they a tablespoonful of lime water once a day in they milk food many novice be in doubt as to the best time to breed from a bull bitch see that oestrum be present before she be fully develop it may be take as practically certain that it be better for she to be allow to breed at she first heat nature have so arrange matter that a bull bitch be not firmly set in she bone until she reach a age of from twelve to eighteen month and therefore she will have less difficulty in give birth to she offspring if she be allow to breed at this time great mortality occur in attempt to breed from maiden bitch exceed three year of age as the writer know to he cost it be desirable in the case of a young bitch have she first litter for she master or mistress to be near she at the time in order to render any necessary assistance but such attention should not be give unless actual necessity arise some bitch with excessive lay-back and shortness of face have at time a difficulty in release the puppy from the membrane in which it be bear and in such a case it be necessary for the owner to open this cover and release the puppy gently shake it about in the box until it cough and begin to breathe the umbilical cord should be sever from the afterbirth about four inch from the puppy and this will dry up and fall away in the course of a couple of day in general it be true economy for the bulldog breeder to provide a foster-mother in readiness for the birth of the expect litter especially be this so in the case of a first litter when the qualification for nursing by the mother be unknown where there be more than five puppy it be also desirable to obtain a foster-mother in order that full nourishment may be give to the litter by both mother the best time of the year for puppy to be bear be in the spring when owe to the approach warm weather they can lead a outdoor life by the time they be six month old they should have sufficient stamen to enable they to withstand the cold of the succeed winter it have be ascertain that bulldog which have be rear out of door be the least liable to suffer from indigestion torpidity of the liver asthma or other chest ailment whilst they invariably have the hardiest constitution bulldog generally require liberal feeding and should have a meal of dry biscuit the first thing in the morning whilst the evening meal should consist of a good stew of butcher 's offal pour over broken biscuit bread or other cereal food in the winter time it be advantageous to soak a tablespoonful of linseed in water overnight and after the pod have open to turn the result jelly into the stew pot this ensure a fine glossy coat and be of value in tone up the intestine care must however be take not to follow this practice to excess in warm weather as the heating nature of the linseed will eventually cause skin trouble with these special point attend to the novice should find no difficulty in successfully become a bulldog fancier owner and breeder in conclusion it can not be too widely know that the bulldog be one of the very few breed which can with perfect safety be trust alone to the mercy of child who naturally in the course of play try the patience and good temper of the firmest friend of man the miniature bulldog fifty or sixty year ago toy -- or rather as a recent edict of the kennel club require they to be dub miniature -- bulldog be common object of the canine country-side in fact you can hardly ever talk for ten minute to any bulldog breeder of old standing without he tell you tall story of the wonderful little bulldog weigh about fifteen or sixteen pound he either know or own in those long-past day prominent among those who make a cult of these bantam be the laceworker of nottingham and many print be extant which bear witness to the excellent little specimen they breed but a wave of unpopularity overwhelm they and they fade across the admirer revive they in england they return _ most _ attractive ` tis true but hamper by many undesirable feature such as bat ear froggy face wave tail and a general lack of bulldog character however the toy bulldog club then start take the dog vigorously in hand and thanks to unceasing effort toy bulldog have always since be cater for at a ever increase number of show they weight after much heated discussion and sundry downs and up be finally fix at twenty-two pound and under the original aim of miniature bulldog -- _ ie _ to look like the larger variety see through the wrong end of a telescope -- if not actually achieve be be rapidly approach and can no longer be look upon as merely the hopeless dream of a few enthusiast to enumerate in detail the miniature bulldog scale of point be quite unnecessary as it be simply that of the big one writ small in other word the general appearance of the miniature bulldog must as nearly as possible resemble that of the big bulldog -- a terse sentence which comprise in itself all that can be say on the subject as companion and friend miniature bulldog be faithful fond and even foolish in they devotion as all true friend should be they be absolutely and invariably good-tempered and as a rule sufficiently fond of the luxury of this life -- not to say greedy -- to be easily cajole into obedience remarkably intelligent and care enough for sport to be sympathetically excite at the sight of a rabbit without degenerate into crank on the subject like terrier take a keen interest in all surround people and object without however give way to ceaseless bark enjoy outdoor exercise without require a exhausting amount they be in every way ideal pet and adapt themselves to town and country alike as puppy they be delicate and require constant care and supervision but that only add a keener zest to the attractive task of breed they the more so owe to the fact that as mother they do not shine be very difficult to manage and generally manifest a strong dislike to rear they own offspring in other respects they be quite hardy little dog and -- one great advantage -- they seldom have distemper cold and damp they particularly dislike especially when puppy and the greatest care should be take to keep they thoroughly dry and warm when very young indeed they can stand and be the better for a extraordinary amount of heat the french bulldog -lrb- bouledogue francai -rrb- there appear to be no doubt that the french bulldog originate in england and be a offshoot of the english miniature variety bulldog not the bulldog one see on the bench to-day but of the tulip-eared and short underjawed specimen which be common in london nottingham birmingham and sheffield in the early ` fifty there be at that time a constant emigration of laceworker from nottingham to the coast town of normandy where lace factory be spring into existence and these immigrant frequently take a bulldog with they to the land of they adoption the converse method be also adopt prior to 1902 french bulldog be import into this country with the object of resuscitate the strain of bantam bulldog which in course of year have be allow to dwindle in number and be in danger of become extinct there be superficial similarity between the english and the french toy bulldog the one distinguish characteristic be that in the french variety the ear be higher on the head and be hold erect until a few year ago the two be interbreed but dispute as to they essential difference lead the kennel club to intervene and the type have since be keep rigidly apart the smart little bat-eared bulldog of france receive recognition under the breed name of bouledogue francais chapter iv the st bernard the history of the st bernard dog would not be complete without reference be make to the noble work that he have do in switzerland he native land : how the hospice st bernard keep a considerable number of dog which be train to go over the mountain with small barrel round they neck contain restorative in the event of they come across any poor traveller who have either lose they way or have be overcome by the cold we have be tell that the intelligent animal save many life in this way the subject of they deliverance often be find entirely bury in the snow handsome as the st bernard be with he attractive color and marking he be a cross-bred dog from the record of old writer it be to be gather that to refill the kennel at the hospice which have be render vacant from the combined catastrophe of distemper and the fall of a avalanche which have sweep away nearly all they hound the monk be compel to have recourse to a cross with the newfoundland and the pyrenean sheepdog the latter not unlike the st bernard in size and appearance then again there be no doubt whatever that at some time the bloodhound have be introduce and it be know for a certainty that almost all the most celebrated st bernard in england at the present time be closely ally to the mastiff the result of all this intermixture of different breed have be the production of a exceedingly fine race of dog which form one of the most attractive feature at we dog show and be individually excellent guard and companion as a companion the st bernard can not be surpass when a large dog be require for the purpose most docile in temperament and disposition he be admirably suit as the associate of a lady or a child the st bernard be sensitive to a degree and seldom forget a insult which he resent with dignity specimen of the breed have occasionally be see that be savage but when this be the case ill-treatment of some sort have assuredly be the provoke cause the dog at the hospice of st bernard be small in comparison with those that be see in england belong to the same race the holy father be more particular about they marking than great size the body color should be brindle or orange tawny with white marking the muzzle white with a line run up between the eye and over the skull join at the back the white collar that encircle the neck down to the front of the shoulder the color round the eye and on the ear should be of a darker shade in the red in the center of the white line at the occiput there should be a spot of color these marking be say to represent the steal chasuble and scapular which form part of the vestment worn by the monk but it be seldom that the marking be so clearly define they be more often white with brindle or orange patch on the body with evenly-marked head in england st bernard be either distinctly rough in coat or smooth but the generality of the hospice dog be break in coat have a texture between the two extreme the property however of the rough and smooth be the same so that the two variety be often breed together and as a rule both texture of coat will be the result of the alliance the late m schumacher a great authority on the breed in switzerland aver that dog with very rough coat be find to be of no use for work on the alp as they thick cover become so load with snow and they foot so clog that they succumb under the weight and perish on that account they be discard by the monk in connection with the origin of the st bernard m schumacher write in a letter to mr j c macdona who be the first to introduce the breed into great britain in any number : accord to the tradition of the holy father of the great saint bernard they race descend from the cross of a bitch -lrb- a bulldog species -rrb- of denmark and a mastiff -lrb- shepherd 's dog -rrb- of the pyrenee the descendant of the cross who have inherit from characterise they have acquire in the space of five century so glorious a notoriety throughout europe that they well merit the name of a distinct race for themselves from the same authority we learn breed or be descend from the bowden dog -lrb- illustration : mr george sinclair 's st bernard ch lord montgomery photograph by c reid wishaw -rrb- the follow be the description of the st bernard as draw up by the member of the st bernard club : \* \* \* \* \* head -- the head should be large and massive the circumference of the skull be more than double the length of the head from nose to occiput from stop to tip of nose should be moderately short full below the eye and square at the muzzle there should be great depth from the eye to the lower jaw and the lip should be deep throughout but not too pendulous from the nose to the stop should be straight and the stop abrupt and well define the skull should be broad and round at the top but not dome with somewhat prominent brow ear -- the ear should be of medium size lie close to the cheek but strong at the base and not heavily feathered eye -- the eye should be rather small and deep set dark in color and not too close together the lower eyelid should droop so as to show a fair amount of haw nose -- the nose should be large and black with well develop nostril the tooth should be level expression -- the expression should betoken benevolence dignity and intelligence neck -- the neck should be lengthy muscular and slightly arch with dewlap develop and the shoulder broad and sloping well up at the withers general description of body -- the chest should be wide and deep and the back level as far as the haunch slightly arch over the loin the rib should be well rounded and carry well back the loin wide and very muscular tail -- the tail should be set on rather high long and in the long-coated variety bushy carry low when in repose and when excite or in motion slightly above the line of the back leg -- the fore-leg should be perfectly straight strong in bone and of good length and the hind-leg very muscular the foot large compact with well-arched toe size -- a dog should be at least 30 inch in height at the shoulder and a bitch 27 inch -lrb- the taller the better provide the symmetry be maintain -rrb- thoroughly well proportioned and of great substance the general outline should suggest great power and capability of endurance coat -- in the long-coated variety the coat should be dense and flat rather fuller round the neck the thigh feathered but not too heavily in the short-coated variety the coat should be dense hard flat and short slightly feathered on thigh and tail color and marking -- the color should be red orange various shades of brindle -lrb- the richer color the better -rrb- or white with patch on body of one of the above name color the marking should be as follow white muzzle white blaze up face white collar round neck white chest foreleg foot and end of tail black shading on face and ear if the blaze be wide and run through to the collar a spot of the body color on the top of the head be desirable the weight of a dog should be from 170 lb to 210 lb of a bitch 160 lb to 190 lb \* \* \* \* newfoundland be essentially black in color but this do not mean that there may be no other color for most black newfoundland have some white mark and these be not consider objectionable so long as and dam but if on the contrary white and black dog be require the proper course be to make judicious cross between the black and white and black variety and destroy any black puppy unless they be black blood would generally produce well-marked white and black newfoundland in mating never be guide solely by the good point of the dog and bitch it be very desirable that they should both have good newfoundland puppy will be find quite hardy and under proper condition of food and quarter they be easy to rear chapter vi the great dane the origin of the great dane like that of many other variety of dog be so obscure that all research have only result in speculative theory but the undoubted antiquity of this dog be prove by the fact that representative of a breed sufficiently similar to be consider he ancestor be find on some of the oldest egyptian monument a few year ago a controversy arise on the breed 's proper designation when the german claim for it the title deutsche dogge germany have several variety of big dog such as the hatzrude saufanger ulmer dogge and rottweiler metzgerhund but contemporaneously with these there exist as in other country in europe another very big breed the instinct and qualification of a sport dog and he have prove himself particularly valuable for hunting big game in hot climate which he stand very well respect the temperament of the great dane and he suitability as a companion writer have go to extreme in praise and condemnation in he favor it must be say that in natural intelligence he be surpass by very few other dog he have a most impose figure and do not like some other big breed slobber from he mouth which be a particularly unpleasant peculiarity when a dog be keep in the house on the other hand it must be admit that with almost the strength of a tiger he combine the excitability of a terrier and no doubt a badly trained great dane be a very dangerous animal it be not sufficient to teach he in the haphazard way which might be successful in get a small dog under control but even as a companion he ought to be train systematically and consider he marked intelligence this be not difficult of accomplishment the great dane attain he full development in about a year and a half to two year and consider that puppy have to build up in that time a very big skeleton and straight limb special attention must be give to the rearing of they the dam whelp frequently eight puppy and sometimes even a few more mr larke 's princess thor have a litter of seventeen but even eight be too great a number for a bitch to suckle in a breed where great size be a desideratum not more than four or at the outside five should be leave with the bitch the other should be put to a foster mother or if they be weakling or foul-marked it be best to destroy they after the puppy be wean they food should be of bone-making quality and they require ample space for exercise and play nothing be worse than to take the youngster for forced march before they bone have become firm before give the description and standard which have be adopt by the great dane club a few remark on some of the lead point will be useful the general characteristic of the great dane be a combination of grace and power and therefore the lightness of the greyhound as well as the heaviness of the mastiff must be avoid the head should be powerful but at the same time show quality by its nice model the eye should be intelligent and vivacious but not have the hard expression of the terrier the distance between the eye be of great importance if too wide apart they give the dog a stupid appearance and if too close he have a treacherous look another very important point be the graceful carriage of the tail when it be curl over the back it make a otherwise handsome dog look mean and a tail that curl at the end like a corkscrew be also very ugly in former time fake be not infrequently resort to to correct a faulty tail carriage but it be easily detect great danes sometimes injure the end of the tail by hit it against a hard substance and those with a good carriage of tail be most liable to this because in excitement they slash it about whereas the faulty position of the tail curl over the back insure immunity from harm until recently british great dane breeder and exhibitor have pay very little attention to color on the principle that like a good horse a good great dane can not be a bad color the english club however have now in this particular also adopt the german standard the orthodox color be brindle fawn blue black and harlequin in the brindle dog the ground color should be any shade from light yellow to dark red-yellow on which the brindle appear in darker stripe the harlequin have on a pure white ground fairly large black patch which must be of irregular shape break up as if they have be tear and not have round outline when brindle great dane be continuously breed together it have be find that they get darker and that the peculiar striping disappear and in that case the introduction of a good fawn into the strain be advisable the constant mating of harlequin have the tendency to make the black patch disappear and the union with a good black great dane will prevent the loss of color the follow be the official description issue by the great dane club : -- \* \* \* \* \* general appearance -- the great dane be not so heavy or massive as the mastiff nor should he too nearly approach the greyhound type remarkable in size and very muscular strongly though elegantly build the head and neck should be carry high and the tail in line with the back or slightly upward but not curl over the hind-quarter elegance of outline and grace of form be most essential to a dane size be absolutely necessary but there must be that alertness of expression and briskness of movement without which the dane character be lose he should have a look of dash and daring of be ready to go anywhere and do anything temperament -- the great dane be good-tempered affectionate and faithful to he master not demonstrative with stranger intelligent courageous and always alert he value as a guard be unrivalled he be easily control when well train but he may grow savage if confine too much keep on chain or ill treated height -- the minimum height of a adult dog should be 30 in that of a bitch 28 in weight -- the minimum weight of a adult dog should be 120 lb that of a bitch 100 lb the greater height and weight to be prefer provide that quality and proportion be also combine head -- take altogether the head should give the idea of great length and strength of jaw the muzzle or foreface be broad and the skull proportionately narrow so that the whole head when view from above and in front have the appearance of equal breadth throughout length of head -- the entire length of head vary with the height of the dog 13 in from the tip of the nose to the back of the occiput be a good measurement for a dog of 32 in at the shoulder the length from the end of the nose to the point between the eye should be about equal or preferably of greater length than from this point to the back of the occiput skull -- the skull should be flat rather than domed and have a slight indentation run up the center the occipital peak not prominent there should be a decide rise or brow over the eye but no abrupt stop between they face -- the face should be chisel well and foreface long of equal depth throughout and well fill in below the eye with no appearance of be pinch muscle of the cheek -- the muscle of the cheek should be quite flat with no lumpiness or cheek bump the angle of the jaw-bone well define lip -- the lip should hang quite square in front form a right angle with the upper line of foreface underline -- the underline of the head view in profile run almost in a straight line from the corner of the lip to the corner of the jawbone allow for the fold of the lip but with no loose skin to hang down jaw -- the lower jaw should be about level or at any rate not project more than the sixteenth of a inch nose and nostril -- the bridge of the nose should be very wide with a slight ridge where the cartilage join the bone -lrb- this be quite a characteristic of the breed -rrb- the nostril should be large wide and open give a blunt look to the nose a butterfly or flesh-coloured nose be not object to in harlequin ear -- the ear should be small set high on the skull and carry slightly erect with the tip fall forward neck -- next to the head the neck be one of the chief characteristic it should be long well arched and quite clean and free from loose skin hold well up snakelike in carriage well set in the shoulder and the junction of head and neck well define shoulder -- the shoulder should be muscular but not load and well slope back with the elbow well under the body so that when view in front the dog do not stand too wide fore-leg and foot -- the fore-leg should be perfectly straight with big flat bone the foot large and round the toe well arch and close the nail strong and curved body -- the body be very deep with rib well spring and belly well draw up back and loin -- the back and loin be strong the latter slightly arch as in the greyhound hind-quarter -- the hind-quarter and thigh be extremely muscular give the idea of great strength and gallop power the second thigh be long and well develop as in a greyhound and the hock set low turn neither out nor in tail -- the tail be strong at the root and end in a fine point reach to or just below the hock it should be carry when the dog be in action in a straight line level with the back slightly curved towards the end but should not curl over the back coat -- the hair be short and dense and sleek-looking and in no case should it incline to coarseness gait or action -- the gait should be lithe springy and free the action high the hock should move very freely and the head should be hold well up color -- the color be brindle fawn blue black and harlequin the harlequin should have jet black patch and spot on a pure white ground gray patch be admissible but not desire but fawn or brindle shades be objectionable \* understand and be as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* general appearance -- the dalmatian should represent a strong muscular and active dog symmetrical in outline and free from coarseness and lumber capable of great endurance combine with a fair amount of speed head -- the head should be of a fair length the skull flat rather broad between the ear and moderately well define at the temple -- _ ie _ exhibit a moderate amount of stop and not in one straight line from the nose to the occiput bone as require in a bull-terrier it should be entirely free from wrinkle muzzle -- the muzzle should be long and powerful the lip clean fitting the jaw moderately close eye -- the eye should be set moderately well apart and of medium size round bright and sparkling with a intelligent expression they color greatly depend on the marking of the dog in the black spotted variety the eye should be dark -lrb- black or dark brown -rrb- in the liver-spotted variety they should be light -lrb- yellow or light brown -rrb- the rim round the eye in the black-spotted variety should be black in the liver-spotted variety brown -- never flesh-colour in either ear -- the ear should be set on rather high of moderate size rather wide at the base and gradually taper to a round point they should be carry close to the head be thin and fine in texture and always spot -- the more profusely the better nose -- the nose in the black-spotted variety should always be black in the liver-spotted variety always brown neck and shoulder -- the neck should be fairly long nicely arched light and taper and entirely free from throatiness the shoulder should be moderately oblique clean and muscular denote speed body back chest and loin -- the chest should not be too wide but very deep and capacious rib moderately well spring never round like barrel hoop -lrb- which would indicate want of speed -rrb- the back powerful loin strong muscular and slightly arched leg and foot -- the leg and foot be of great the hind-leg the muscle should be clean though well-defined the hock well let down nail -- the nail in the black-spotted variety should be black and white in the liver-spotted variety brown and white tail -- the tail should not be too long strong at the insertion and gradually taper towards the end free from coarseness it should not be insert too low down but carry with a slight curve upward and never curl it should be spot the more profusely the better coat -- the coat should be short hard dense and fine sleek and glossy in appearance but neither woolly nor silky color and marking -- these be most important point the ground color in both variety should be pure white very decide and not intermix the color of the spot of the black-spotted variety should be black the deeper and richer the black the better in the liver-spotted variety they should be brown the spot should not intermingle but be as round and well-defined as possible the more distinct the better in size they should be from that of a sixpence to a florin the spot on head face ear leg tail and extremity to be smaller than those on the body weight -- dog 55 lb bitch 50 lb chapter viii the collie the townsman who know the shepherd 's dog only as he be to be see out of he true element thread he confine way through crowd street where sheep be not can have small appreciation of he wisdom and he sterling worth to know he properly one need to see he at work in a country where sheep abound to watch he adroitly round up he scattered charge on a wide-stretching moorland gather the wander wether into close order and drive they before he in unbroken company to the fold handle the stubborn pack in a narrow lane or hold they in a corner of a field immobile under the spell of he vigilant eye he be at he best as a worker conscious of the responsibility repose in he a marvel of generalship gentle judicious slow to anger quick to action the priceless helpmeet of he master -- the most useful member of all the tribe of dog few dog possess the fertile resourceful brain of the collie he can be train to perform the duty of other breed he make a excellent sport dog and can be teach to do the work of the pointer and the decide preference it be however as a assistant to the flock-master the farmer the butcher and the drover that the collie take he most appropriate place in every-day life the shepherd on he daily round a score of man little be know with certainty of the origin of the collie but he cunning and he outward appearance would seem to indicate a relationship with the wild dog buffon be of opinion that he be the true dog of nature the stock and model of the whole canine species he consider the sheepdog superior in instinct and intelligence to all other breed and that with a character in which education have comparatively little share he be the only animal bear perfectly train for the service of man one of the most perfect work collie in scotland to-day be the old-fashioned black and white type which be the most popular among the shepherd of scotland at the show this type of dog be invariably at the top of the class he be consider the most tractable and be certainly the most agile second to this type in favor be the smooth-coated variety a very hard useful dog well adapt for hill work and usually very fleet of foot he be not so sweet in temper as the black and white and be slow to make friend in the ettrick and yarrow district the smooth be a popular sheepdog the shepherd maintain that he climb the hill more swiftly than the rough and in the heavy snowstorm he clean unfeathered leg do not collect and carry the snow he have a fuller coat than the show specimen usually carry but he have the same type of head eye and ear only not so well develop then there be the scottish bearded or highland collie less popular still with the flock-master a hardy-looking dog in outward style but soft in temperament and many of they make better cattle than sheep dog this dog and the old english sheepdog be much alike in appearance but that the beard be a more racy animal with a head resemble that of the dandie dinmont rather than the square head of the bobtail the strong-limbed bearded collie be capable of get through a good day 's work but be not so steady nor so wise as the old-fashioned black and white or even the smooth coated variety he be a favorite with the butcher and drover who have sometimes a herd of troublesome cattle to handle and he be well suit to rough and rocky ground active in movement and as sure-footed as the wild goat he can endure cold and wet without discomfort and can live on the highland hill when other less sturdy would succumb in the standard adopt for judge the breed many point be give for good leg and foot bone body and coat while head and ear be not of great importance movement size and general appearance have much weight the color be vary in this breed cream-coloured specimen be not uncommon and snow white with orange or black marking may often be see but the popular color be grizzly gray unfortunately the coat of many be far too soft and the undercoat be frequently absent work trial to test the skill of the sheepdog have become frequent fixture among shepherd and farmer within recent year and these competition have do much towards the improvement of the work quality of the collie in general the excel competitor at work trial be the rough-coated black and white collie the smooth-coated variety and the beardie be less frequent winner the handsome and distinguished gentleman of the ch wishaw leader type be seldom see on the rough-and-tumble-looking customer with he coat as nature leave it chapter x the chow chow the chow chow be a dog of great versatility he be a bear sportsman and love a open-air life -- a warrior chapter xi the poodle the poodle be commonly acknowledge to be the most wisely intelligent of all member of the canine race he be a scholar and a gentleman but in spite of he claim of long descent and he extraordinary natural cleverness he have never be widely popular in this country as the collie and the fox-terrier be popular there be a general belief that he be a fop whose time be largely occupy in personal embellishment and that he require a great deal of individual attention in the matter of he toilet it may be true that to keep he in exhibition order and perfect cleanliness he owner have need to devote more consideration to he than be necessary in the case of many breed but in other respects he give very little trouble and all who be attach to he be consistent in they opinion that there be no dog so intensely interesting and responsive as a companion he quality of mind and he acute power of reasoning be indeed so great that there be something almost human in he attractiveness and he devotion he aptitude in learning be never deny and many be the story tell of he marvellous talent and versatility not merely as a showman 's dog have he distinguish himself he be something more than a mountebank of the booth train to walk the tight rope and stand on he head he be a adept at perform trick but it be he alertness of brain that place he apart from other animal there be the example of the famous munito who in 1818 perplex the parisian by he cleverness with play card and he intricate arithmetical calculation pari be formerly the home of most of the learn poodle and one remember the instance of the poodle of the pont neuf who have the habit of dirty the boot of the passer-by in order that he master -- a shoe-black station half-way across the bridge -- might enjoy the profit of clean they in belgium poodle be systematically train to smuggle valuable lace which be wind round they shaven body and cover with a false skin these dog be school to a dislike of all man in uniform and consequently on they journey between mechlin and the coast they always give a wide berth to the custom officer on the continent poodle of the larger kind be often use for draught work there can be little doubt that the breed originate in germany where it be know as the _ pudel _ and class as the _ cani familiari aquaticus _ in form and coat he would seem to be closely related to the old water-dog and the resemblance between a brown poodle and a irish water spaniel be remarkable the poodle be no longer regard as a sport dog but at one period he be train to retrieve waterfowl and he still on occasion display a eager fondness for the water throughout europe and in the united state -- wherever these dog be keep -- it be usual to clip the coat on the face the leg and the hinder part of the body leave tuft of hair on the thigh and a ring of hair on the pastern the origin and purpose of the custom be not apparent but now that poodle be almost always keep as house dog this mode of ornamentation at least commend itself by reduce the labor of daily groom if the coat be to be maintain in good condition and the dog to be a pleasant associate the profuse and long coat of this dog have the peculiarity that if not keep constantly brush out it twist up into little cord which increase in length as the new hair grow and cling about it the unshed old hair and the new growth entwine together thus become distinct rope-like cord eventually if these cord be not cut short or accidentally tear off they drag along the ground and so prevent the poor animal from move with any degree of comfort or freedom some few owner who admire and cultivate these long cord keep they tie up in bundle on the dog 's back but so unnatural and unsightly a method of burden the animal be not to be commend corded poodle be very showy and from the remarkable appearance of the coat attract a great deal of public attention when exhibit at show but they have lose popularity among most fancier and have become few in number owe to the obvious fact that it be impossible to make pet of they or keep they in the house the reason of this be that the coat must from time to time be oil in order to keep the cord supple and prevent they from snap and of course as they coat can not be brush the only way of keep the dog clean be to wash he which with a cord poodle be a lengthy and laborious process further the coat take hour to dry and unless the newly wash dog be keep in a warm room he be very liable to catch cold the result be that the coat of cord poodle be almost invariably dirty and somewhat smelly at one time it be suggest that corded and non-corded be two distinct breed but it be now generally accept that the coat of every well-bred poodle will if allow develop cord curly poodle on the other hand have advance considerably in favor they coat should be keep regularly brush and comb and if wash occasionally they will always be smart and clean and pleasant companion in the house the four color usually consider correct be black white brown and blue white poodle be consider the most intelligent and it be certain that professional trainer of perform dog prefer the white variety the black come next in the order of intelligence and easily surpass the brown and blue which be somewhat lack in true poodle character no strict line be draw as regard brown and all shades range from cream to dark brown be class as brown mr robert long a few year ago startle she fellow-enthusiast by exhibit some parti-coloured specimen but they be regard as freak and do not become popular the point to be look for in choose a poodle be that he should be a lively active dog with a long fine head a dark oval eye with a bright alert expression short in the back not leggy but by no means low on the ground with a good loin carry he tail well up the coat should be profuse all one color very curly and rather wiry to the touch if you buy a poodle puppy you will find it like other intelligent and active youngster full of mischief the great secret in training he be first to gain he affection with firmness kindness and perseverance you can then teach he almost anything the most lively and excitable dog be usually the easiest to train it be advantageous to teach you dog when you give he he meal of biscuit let he have the food piece by piece as a reward when each trick be duly perform never attempt to teach he two new trick at a time and when instruct he in a new trick let he always go through he old one first make it a invariable rule never to be beat by he if -- as frequently be the case with you dog -- he decline to perform a trick do not pass it over or allow he to substitute another he like better but when you see he obstinately refuse punish he by put away the coveted food for a hour or two if he once see he can tire you out you will have no further authority over he while if you be firm he will not hold out against you long it be a bad plan to make a dog repeat too frequently a trick which he obviously dislike and insistence on you part may do great harm the poodle be exceptionally sensitive and be far more efficiently teach when treat as a sensible be rather than as a mere quadrupedal automaton he will learn twice as quickly if he master can make he understand the reason for perform a task the whip be of little use when a lesson be to the dog have be out in the rain and get he coat soak or if he have be wash or allow to jump into a pond you must take care not to leave he in a cold place or to lie inactive before he be perfectly dry most poodle be keep in the house or in enclosed kennel well protect from draught and moisture and there be no difficulty in so keep they as they be naturally obedient and easily teach to be clean in the house and to be regular in they habit the coat of a curly poodle should be keep fleecy and free from tangle by be periodically comb and brush the groom keep the skin clean and healthy and frequent wash even for a white dog be not necessary the dog will of course require clipping from time to time in pari at present it be the fashion to clip the greater part of the body and hind-quarter but the the irish wolfhound it be now some thirty year since a important controversy be carry on in the column of _ the live stock journal _ on the nature and history of the great irish wolfhound the chief disputant in the discussion be captain g a graham of dursley mr g w hickman mr f adcock and the rev m b wynn and the main point as issue be whether the dog then imperfectly know as the irish wolfdog be a true descendant of the ancient _ cani graius hibernicus _ or whether it be a mere manufactured mongrel owe its origin to a admixture of the great dane and the dog of the pyrenee modify and bring to type by a cross with the highland deerhound it be not doubt -- indeed history and tradition clearly attest -- that there have exist in early time in ireland a very large and rugged hound of greyhound form whose vocation it be to hunt the wolf the red deer and the fox it be assuredly know to the roman and there can be little doubt that the huge dog samr which jarl gunnar get from the irish king myrkiarton in the tenth century and take back with he to norway be one of this breed but it be suppose by many to have become extinct soon after the disappearance of the last wolf in ireland and it be the endeavor of captain graham to demonstrate that specimen although admittedly degenerate be still to be find and that they be capable of be restore to a semblance of the original type at the time when he enter into the controversy captain graham have be actively interesting himself for something like a score of year in the resuscitation of the breed and he patience have be well reward by the year 1881 the irish wolfhound have be practically restore although it have take close upon a quarter of a century to produce the magnificent champion cotswold and cotswold patricium race it seem extraordinary that so little should have be accurately know and record of a dog which at one time must have be a familiar figure in the hall of the irish king it be no mere mythical animal like the heraldic griffin but a actual sport dog which be accept as a national emblem of the emerald isle associate with the harp and the shamrock as regard the origin of the irish wolfhound
