sweep with a slight curve towards the extremity the minimum height and weight of dog should be 31 inch and 120 pound of bitch 28 inch and 90 pound anything below this should be debar from competition great size include height at shoulder and proportionate length of body be the desideratum to be aim at and it be desire firmly to establish a race that shall average from 32 inch to 34 inch in dog show the requisite power activity courage and symmetry head -- long the frontal bone of the forehead very slightly raise and very little indentation between the eye skull not too broad muzzle long and moderately point ear small and greyhound-like in carriage neck -- rather long very strong and muscular well arched without dewlap and loose skin about the throat chest -- very deep breast wide back -- rather long than short loin arch tail -- long and slightly curve of moderate thickness and well cover with hair belly -- well draw up fore-quarter -- shoulder muscular give breadth of chest set sloping elbow well under neither turn inwards nor outwards leg -- forearm muscular and the whole leg strong and quite straight hind-quarter -- muscular thigh and second thigh long and strong as in the greyhound and hock well let down and turn neither in nor out foot -- moderately large and round neither turn inwards nor outwards toe well arch and close nail very strong and curved hair -- rough and hard on body leg and head especially wiry and long over eye and under jaw color and marking -- the recognize color be gray brindle red black pure white fawn or any color that appear in the deerhound fault -- too light or heavy in head too highly arched frontal bone large ear and hang flat to the face short neck full dewlap too narrow or too broad a chest sunken and hollow or quite level back bent fore-leg over-bent fetlock twisted foot spread toe too curly a tail weak hind-quarter cow hock and a general want of muscle too short in body chapter xvi the deerhound the deerhound be one of the most decorative of dog impressively stately and picturesque wherever he be see whether it be amid the surroundings of the baronial hall recline at luxurious length before the open hearth in the fitful light of the log fire that flicker on polished armor and tarnish tapestry out in the open strain at the leash as he scent the dewy air or gracefully bound over the purple of he native hill grace and majesty be in he every movement and attitude and even to the most prosaic mind there be about he the inseparable glamour of feudal romance and poetry he be at he best alert in the excitement of the chase but all too rare now be the inspiring sight that once be common among the mountain of morven and the glen of argyll of the deep-voiced hound speeding in pursuit of he antlered prey race he at full stretch along the mountain 's ridge or bay he at last in the fastness of darksome corrie or deep ravine go be the good romantic day of stalk beloved by scrope the highland have lose they loneliness and the invention of the modern gunsmith have rob one of the grandest of hunting dog of he glory relegate he to the life of a pedestrian pet whose highest dignity be the winning of a pecuniary prize under kennel club rule historian of the deerhound associate he with the original irish wolfdog of whom he be obviously a close relative and it be sure that when the wolf still linger in the land it be the frequent quarry of the highland as of the hibernian hound legend have it that prince ossian son of fingal king of morven hunt the wolf with the gray long-bounding dog swift-footed luath and white-breasted bran be among the name of ossian 's hound i be dispose to affirm that the old irish wolfhound and the highland deerhound be not only intimately ally in form and nature but that they be two strain of a identical breed alter only in size by circumstance and environment whatever the source of the highland deerhound and at whatever period it become distinct from its now larger irish relative it be recognize as a native dog in scotland in very early time and it be distinguish as be superior in strength and beauty to the hound of the pict from remote day the scottish noble cherish they strain of deerhound seek glorious sport in the highland forest the red deer belong by inexorable law to the king of scotland and great drive which often last for several leave in the hand of retainer who thus replenish they chief 's larder the revival of deerstalk date back hardly further than a hundred year it reach its greatest popularity in the highland at the time inch in height two historic feat of strength and endurance illustrate the tenacity of the deerhound at work a brace of half-bred dog name percy and dougla the property of mr scrope keep a stag at bay from Saturday night to Monday morning and the pure breed bran by himself pull down two unwounded stag one carry ten and the other eleven tine these of course be record performance but they demonstrate the possibility of the deerhound when train to he natural sport -lrb- illustration : mr armstrong 's deerhound ch talisman -rrb- driving be commonly resort to in the extensive forest but nowadays when forest be sub-divide into limited shooting the deer be seldom move from they home preserve whilst with the use of improve telescope and the small-bore rifle stalk have go out of fashion with gun have a muzzle velocity of 2500 foot per second it be no longer necessary for sportsman stealthily to stalk they game to come within easy range and as for hound they have become a doubtful appendage to the chase primarily and essentially the deerhound belong to the order _ agaseus _ hunting by sight and not by scent and although he may indeed occasionally put he nose to the ground yet he power of scent be not remarkable he vocation therefore have undergo a change and it be recently ascertain that of sixty deer forest there be only six upon which deerhound be keep for sport purpose happily the grace and elegance and even more so for he faithful and affectionate nature sir walter scott declare that he be a most perfect creature of heaven and when one see he represent in so beautiful a great size rather than to preserve the genuine type but this error have be sufficiently correct with the result that symmetry and elegance conjoin with the desire attribute of speed be not sacrifice the quality aim at now be a height of something less than 30 inch and a weight not greater than 105 lb with straight fore-leg and short cat-like foot a deep chest with broad powerful loin slightly arched and strength of hind-quarter with well-bent stifle and the hock well let down straight stifle be objectionable give a stilty appearance thick shoulder be equally a blemish to be avoid as also a too great heaviness of bone the follow be the accept standard of merit \* \* \* \* \* head -- the head should be broadest at the ear taper slightly to the eye with the muzzle taper more decidedly to the nose the muzzle should be pointed but the tooth and lip level the head should be long the skull flat rather than round with a very slight rise over the eye but with nothing approach a stop the skull should be coat with moderately long hair which be softer than the rest of the coat the nose should be black -lrb- though in some blue-fawn the color be blue -rrb- and slightly aquiline in the lighter-coloured dog a black muzzle be prefer there should be a good moustache of rather silky hair and a fair beard ear -- the ear should be set on high and in repose fold back like the greyhound 's though raise above the head in excitement without lose the fold and even in some case semi-erect a prick ear be bad a big thick ear hang flat to the head or heavily coated with long hair be the worst of fault the ear should be soft glossy and like a mouse 's coat to the touch and the smaller it be the better it should have no long coat or long fringe but there be often a silky silvery coat on the body of the ear and the tip whatever the general color the ear should be black or dark-coloured neck and shoulder -- the neck should be long -- that be of the length that befit the greyhound character of the dog a over-long neck be not necessary nor desirable for the dog be not require to stoop in he work like a greyhound and it must be remember that the mane which every good specimen should have detract from the apparent length of neck moreover a deerhound require a very strong neck to hold a stag the nape of the neck should be very prominent where the head be set on and the throat should be clean-cut at the angle and prominent the shoulder should be well slope the blade well back with not too much width between they loaded and straight shoulder be very bad fault stern -- stern should be tolerably long taper and reach to within 1-1\/2 inch of the ground and about 1-1\/2 inch below the hock when the dog be still drop perfectly straight down or curve when in motion it should be curve when excite in no case to be lift out of the line of the back it should be well cover with hair on the inside thick and wiry underside longer and towards the end a slight fringe be not objectionable a curl or ring tail be very undesirable eye -- the eye should be dark : generally they be dark brown or hazel a very light eye be not like the eye be moderately full with a soft look in repose but a keen far-away gaze when the dog be rouse the rim of the eyelid should be black body -- the body and general formation be that of a greyhound of larger size and bone chest deep rather than broad but not too narrow and flat-sided the loin well arched and droop to the tail a straight back be not desirable this formation be unsuitable for go uphill and very unsightly leg and foot -- the leg should be broad and flat a good broad forearm and elbow be desirable fore-leg of course as straight as possible foot close and compact with well-arched toe the hind-quarter droop and as broad and powerful as possible the hip be set wide apart the hind-leg should be well bent at the stifle with great length from the hip to the hock which should be broad and flat cow hock weak pastern straight stifle and splay foot be very bad fault coat -- the hair on the body neck and quarter should be harsh and wiry and about 3 inch or 4 inch long that on the head breast and belly be much softer there should be a slight hairy fringe on the inside of the fore and hind-leg but nothing approach to the feathering of a collie the deerhound should be a shaggy dog but not over coat a woolly coat be bad some good strain have a slight mixture of silky coat with the hard which be preferable to a woolly coat but the proper covering be a thick close-lying ragged coat harsh or crisp to the touch color -- color be much a matter of fancy but there be no manner of doubt that the dark blue-grey be the most preferred next come the darker and lighter grey or brindle the darkest be generally prefer yellow and sandy-red or red-fawn especially with black point -- _ ie _ ear and muzzle -- be also in equal estimation this be the color of the oldest known strain the mcneil and the chesthill menzy white be condemn by all the old authority but a white chest and white toe occur as they do in a great many of the darkest-coloured dog be not so greatly object to but the less the better as the deerhound be a self-coloured dog a white blaze on the head or a white collar should entirely disqualify in other case though passable a attempt should be make to get rid of white marking the less white the better but a slight white tip to the stern occur in the best strain height of dog -- from 28 inch to 30 inch or even more if there be symmetry without coarseness which however be rare height of bitch -- from 26 inch upwards there can be no objection to a bitch be large unless she be too coarse as even at she greatest height she do not approach that of the dog and therefore could not well be too big for work as over-big dog be besides a big bitch be good for breed and keep up the size weight -- from 85 pound to 105 pound in dog from 65 pound to 80 pound in bitch \* \* \* \* \* among the more kenilworth and ferraline she ayrshire be consider by some judge to be the most perfect deerhound exhibit for some time past he be somewhat large perhaps but he be throughout a hound of excellent quality and character have a most typical head with lovely eye and expression perfect front foot and hind-quarter other judge would give the palm to mr harry rawson 's st ronan 's ranger who be certainly difficult to excel in all the characteristic most desirable in the breed chapter xvii the borzoi or russian wolfhound of the many foreign variety of the dog that have be introduce into this country within recent year there be not one among the larger breed that have make greater headway in the public favor than the borzoi or russian wolfhound nor be this to be wonder at the most graceful and elegant of all breed combine symmetry with strength the wearer of a lovely silky coat that a toy dog might envy the length of head possess by no other breed -- all go to make the borzoi the favorite he have become he be essentially what we american cousin would call a spectacular dog give for example the best team of terrier and a fifth-rate team of borzoi which attract the more attention and admiration from the man in the street which do he turn again to look at not the terrier add to this that the borzoi make a capital house dog be as a rule affectionate and a good companion it be not to be wonder at that he have attain the dignified position in the canine world which he now hold in he native country the borzoi be employ as he english name imply in hunting the wolf and also smaller game include fox and hare several method of hunting the larger game be adopt one form be as follow wolf be report to be present in the neighborhood the hunter set out on horseback each hold in he left hand a leash of three borzoi as nearly match as possible in size speed and color arrive at the scene of action the chief huntsman station the hunter at separate point every hundred yard or so round the wood a pack of hound be send in to draw the quarry and on the wolf break cover the nearest hunter slip he dog these endeavor to seize they prey by the neck where they hold he until the hunter arrive throw himself from he horse and with he knife put a end to the fray another method be to advance across the open country at interval of about two hundred yard slip the dog at any game they may put up trial be also hold in russium these take place in a large rail enclosure the wolf be bring in cart similar to we deer cart in this case a brace of dog be loose on the wolf the whole merit of the course be when the hound can overtake the wolf and pin he to the ground so that the keeper can secure he alive it follow therefore that in this case also the hound must be of equal speed so that they reach the wolf simultaneously one dog would of course be unable to hold he naturally the dog have to be train to the work for which purpose the best wolf be take alive and send to the kennel where the young dog be teach to pin he in such a manner that he can not turn and use he tooth there seem to be no reason why the borzoi should not be use for course in this country one of the first example of the breed exhibit in england be own by messr hill and ashton of sheffield about 1880 at which time good specimen be import by the rev j c macdona and lady emily peel whose sandringham and czar excited general admiration it be then know as the siberian wolfhound some year later the duchess of newcastle obtain several fine dog and from this stock she grace champion the breed have become as fashionable in the united state as in great britain and some excellent specimen be to be see at the annual show at madison square garden to take the point of the breed in detail the description of the perfect borzoi be as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* head -- this should be long lean and well balanced and the length from the tip of the nose to the eye must be the same as from the eye to the occiput a dog may have a long head but the length may be all in front of the eye the head of this breed have greatly improve the last few year fewer apple-headed specimen and more of the desire triangular head be see the skull should be flat and narrow the stop not perceptible the muzzle long and taper too much stress can not be lay on the importance of the head be well fill up before the eye the head from forehead to nose should be so fine that the direction of the bone and principal vein can be see clearly and in profile should appear rather roman nosed bitch should be even narrower in head than dog the eye should be dark expressive almond shape and not too far apart the ear like those of a greyhound small thin and place well back on the head with the tip when throw back almost touch behind the occiput it be not a fault if the dog can raise he ear erect when excite or look after game although some english judge dislike this frequent characteristic the head should be carry somewhat low with the neck continue the line of the back shoulder -- clean and sloping well back _ ie _ the shoulder blade should almost touch one another chest -- deep and somewhat narrow it must be capacious but the capacity must be get from depth and not from barrel rib -- a bad fault in a run hound back -- rather bony and free from any cavity in the spinal column the arch in the back be more marked in the dog than in the bitch loin -- broad and very powerful show plenty of muscular development thigh -- long and well develop with good second thigh the muscle in the borzoi be longer than in the greyhound rib -- slightly spring very deep reach to the elbow fore-leg -- lean and straight see from the front they should be narrow and from the side broad at the shoulder and narrow gradually down to the foot the bone appear flat and not round as in the foxhound hind-leg -- the least thing under the body when stand still not straight and the stifle slightly bent they should of course be straight as regard each other and not cow-hocked but straight hind-leg imply a want of speed foot -- like those of the deerhound rather long the toe close together and well arched coat -- long silky not woolly either flat wavy or curly on the head ear and front-leg it should be short and smooth on the neck the frill should be profuse and rather curly on the chest and the rest of the body the tail and hind-quarter it should be long the fore-leg be well feathered tail -- long well feathered and not gaily carry it should be carry well down almost touch the ground height -- dog from 29 inch upward at shoulder bitch from 27 inch upward -lrb- originally 27 inch and 26 inch alter at a general meeting of the borzoi club hold February 1906 -rrb- fault -- head short and thick too much stop parti-coloured nose eye too wide apart heavy ear heavy shoulder wide chest barrel rib dew-claws elbow turn out wide behind also light eye and over or undershot jaw color -- the club standard make no mention of color white of course should predominate fawn lemon orange brindle blue slate and black marking be meet with too much of the latter or black and tan marking be dislike whole color dog be also see \* \* \* \* \* the foregoing description embody the standard of point as lay down and adopt by the borzoi club interpolate with some remark for the further guidance of the novice the borzoi club be found in 1892 and now consist of about fifty member with the duke and duchess of newcastle as joint-president it do much good work for the breed guaranteeing class at show where otherwise few or none would be give encourage the breeding of high-class borzoi by offer its valuable challenge cup and other special prize and generally look after the interest of the breed although the club standard of height have be raise from 27 and 26 inch to 29 and 27 inch for dog and bitch respectively it must be bear in mind that the best dog of to-day far exceed these measurement and unless _ exceptionally _ good in other point a dog of 29 inch at shoulder would stand little or no chance in the show under the majority of english judge indeed bitch of 29 to 30 inch be by no means uncommon not many of we can afford to start at the top of the tree and except for the favored few to whom money be no object and who can buy ready-made champion there be no better way of start a kennel than to purchase a really good bitch one say capable of win at all but the more important show she must be of good pedigree strong and healthy such a one ought to be obtain for p15 upward mate she to the best dog whose blood nick suitably with hers but do not waste time and money breed from fourth-rate stud dog for if you do it be certain you will only meet with disappointment on the other friend who understand the breed -rrb- it be a fact that even a cast off from a good strain that have be breed for certain point for year be more likely to turn out a better dog than a pup whose dam have be mate haphazard to some dog who may or may not have be a good one big kennel also generally possess the best bitch and breed from they and the bitch be quite as important a factor as the sire if however you prefer to rely on you own judgment and wish to choose a puppy yourself from a litter select the one with the longest head biggest bone smallest ear and longest tail or as many of these quality as you can find combine in one individual coat be a secondary matter in quite a young pup here one should be guide by the coat of the sire and dam still choose a pup with a heavy coat if possible although when this puppy coat be cast the dog may not grow so good as one as some of the litter who in early life be smoother as regard size a borzoi pup of three month should measure about 19 inch at the shoulder at six month about 25 inch and at nine month from 27 to 29 inch after ten or twelve month growth be very slow although some continue add to they height until they be a year and a half old they will of course increase in girth of chest and develop muscle until two year old a borzoi may be consider in its prime at from three to four year of age as regard price from p5 to p10 be not too much to pay for a really good pup of about eight to ten week old if you pay less you will probably get only a second-rate one have purchase you puppy there be three principal item to be consider if you intend to rear he well firstly he diet must be varied secondly the pup must have unlimited exercise and never be keep on the chain thirdly internal parasite must be keep in check for young puppy ruby worm cure be most efficacious and do not distress the patient food should be give at regular interval -- not less frequently than five time a day to newly wean puppy -- and may consist of porridge bread and milk raw meat minced fine and any table scrap with plenty of new milk well-boiled paunch be also greatly appreciate and be easily digest may be give freely one important part of the puppy 's education that must by no means be neglect be to accustom he to go on the collar and lead borzoi pup be as a rule extremely nervous and it require great patience in some case to train they to the lead short lesson should be give when about four month old if you can induce the puppy to think it be a new game well and good -- he will take to it naturally but once he look upon it as something to be dread it mean hour of patient work to break he in if you decide on commence with a brood bitch see that she be dose for worm before visit the dog that she be in good hard condition -- not fat however and if possible accompany she yourself and see she mate for the first week rather less than she usual quantity of food should be give afterwards feed as she appetite dictate but do not let she get too fat or she may have a bad time when whelp for two day before the puppy be due give sloppy but nourishing diet and this should be continue give slightly warm for four or five day after the pup be bear borzois as a rule make excellent mother but to rear they well they should not be allow to suckle more than five -- or if a strong big bitch six -- pup if the litter require from that of other large breed chapter xviii the greyhound the greyhound be the oldest and most conservative of all dog and he type have alter singularly little during the seven thousand year cup and the field trial challenge cup for competition amongst its member besides have liberally support all the lead show hence it have rightly come to be regard as the only authority from which a acceptable and official dictum for the guidance of other can emanate the following be the standard of point issue by the english setter club : -- \* \* \* \* \* head -- the head should be long and lean with well-defined stop the skull oval from ear to ear show plenty of brain room and with a well-defined occipital protuberance the muzzle moderately deep and fairly square from the stop to the point of the nose should be long the nostril wide and the jaw of nearly equal length flew not too pendulous the color of the nose should be black or dark or light liver accord to the color of the coat the eye should be bright mild and intelligent and of a dark hazel color the darker the better the ear of moderate length set on low and hang in neat fold close to the cheek the tip should be velvety the upper part clothe with fine silky hair neck -- the neck should be rather long muscular and lean slightly arch at the crest and clean cut where it join the head towards the shoulder it should be larger and very muscular not throaty with any pendulosity below the throat but elegant and bloodlike in appearance body -- the body should be of moderate length with shoulder well set back or oblique back short and level loin wide slightly arched strong and muscular chest deep in the brisket with good round widely-sprung rib deep in the back rib -- that be well rib up leg and foot -- the stifle should be well bent and ragged thigh long from hip to hock the forearm big and very muscular the elbow well let down pastern short muscular and straight the foot very close and compact and well protect by hair between the toe tail -- the tail should be set on almost in a line with the back medium length not curly or ropy to be slightly curved or scimitar-shaped but with no tendency to turn upward the flag or feather hanging in long pendant flake the feather should not commence at the root but slightly below and increase in length to the middle then gradually taper off towards the end and the hair long bright soft and silky wavy but not curly coat and feathering -- the coat from the back of the head in a line with the ear ought to be slightly wavy long and silky which should be the case with the coat generally the breeches and fore-leg nearly down to the foot should be well feathered color and marking -- the color may be either black and white lemon and white liver and white or tricolor -- that be black white and tan those without heavy patch of color on the body but fleck all over prefer \* \* \* \* \* ii the irish setter -- though this variety have not attain such -- the head should be long and lean the skull oval -lrb- from ear to ear -rrb- have plenty of brain room and with well-defined occipital protuberance brow raise show stop the muzzle moderately deep and fairly square at the end from the stop to the point of the nose should be fairly long the nostril wide and the jaw of nearly equal length flew not to be pendulous the color of the nose dark mahogany or dark walnut and that of the eye -lrb- which ought not to be too large -rrb- rich hazel or brown the ear to be of moderate size fine in texture set on low well back and hang in a neat fold leg and foot -- the hind-leg from hip to hock should be long and muscular from hock to heel short and strong the stifle and hock joint well bent and not inclined either in or out the fore-leg should be straight and sinewy have plenty of bone with elbow free well let down and like the hock not incline either in or out the foot small very firm toe strong close together and arched tail -- the tail should be of moderate length set on rather low strong at root and taper to a fine point to be carry as nearly as possible on a level or below the back coat -- on the head front of leg and tip of ear the coat should be short and fine but on all other part of the body and leg it ought to be of moderate length flat and as free as possible from curl or wave feathering -- the feather on the upper portion of the ear should be long and silky on the back of fore and hind-leg long and fine a fair amount of hair on the belly form a nice fringe which may extend on chest and throat foot to be well feathered between the toe tail to have a nice fringe of moderately long hair decrease in length as it approach the point all feather to be as straight and as flat as possible color and marking -- the color should be a rich golden chestnut with no trace whatever of black white on chest throat or toe or a small star on the forehead or a narrow streak or blaze on the nose or face not to disqualify \* the spaniel family -- the spaniel family be without any doubt one of the most important of the many group which be include in the canine race not only on account of its undoubted antiquity and compare with other family its well authenticated lineage but also because of its many branch and subdivision range in size from the majestic and massive clumber to the diminutive toy which we be accustom to associate with fair lady ' lap and gaily-decked pen at we big dog show moreover the different variety of setter undoubtedly derive they origin from the same parent stock since we find they describe by the earlier sport writer as set or crouch spaniel in contradistinction to the finding or spring spaniel who flush the game he find without set or point it as time go on the setting variety be no doubt breed larger and longer in the leg with a view to increase pace but the spaniel-like head and coat still remain to prove the near connection between the two breed all the different variety of spaniel both sport and toy have with the exception of the clumber and the irish water spaniel -lrb- who be not despite he name a true spaniel at all -rrb- a common origin though at a very early date we find they divide into two group -- viz land and water spaniel and these two be keep distinct and breed to develop those point which be most essential for they different sphere of work the earliest mention of spaniel to be find in english literature be contain in the celebrated master of game the work of edward plantagenet second duke of york and master of game to he uncle henry iv to whom the work be dedicate it be write between the year 1406 and 1413 and although none of the mss of which some sixteen be in existence be date this date can be fairly accurately fix as the author be appoint master of game in the former and kill at agincourt in the latter year he chapter on spaniel however be mainly a translation from the equally celebrated livre de chasse of gaston comte de foix generally know as gaston phoebus which be write in 1387 so that we may safely assume that spaniel be well know and habitually use as aid to the chase both in france and england as early as the middle of the fourteenth century in the eighteenth and early part of the nineteenth century the spaniel be describe by many writer on sport subject but there be a great similarity in most of these account each author apparently have be content to repeat in almost identical language what have be say upon the subject by he predecessor without import any originality or opinion of he own many of these work personal appearance of this quaint-looking dog the point regard as essential be as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* color -- the color should always be a rich dark liver or puce without any white at all any white except the slightest of shirt front should disqualify the _ nose _ of course should conform to the coat in color and be dark brown head -- the head should have a capacious skull fairly but not excessively domed with plenty of brain room it should be surmount with a regular topknot of curly hair a _ most important _ and distinctive point this topknot should _ never _ be square cut or like a poodle 's wig but should grow down to a well define point between the eye eye -- the eye should be small dark and set obliquely like a chinaman 's ear -- the ear should be long strong in leather low set heavily ringleted and from 18 to 24 inch long accord to size muzzle and jaw -- the muzzle and jaw should be long and strong there should be a decide stop but not so pronounced as to make the brow or forehead prominent neck -- the neck should be fairly long and very muscular shoulder -- the shoulder should be slope most irish water spaniel have bad straight shoulder a defect which should be breed out chest -- the chest be deep and usually rather narrow but should not be so narrow as to constrict the heart and lung back and loin -- the back and loin strong and arched fore-leg -- the fore-leg straight and well bone heavily feathered or ringleted all over hind-leg -- the hind-leg with hock set very low stifle rather straight feathered all over except inside from the hock down which part should be cover with short hair -lrb- a most distinctive point -rrb- foot -- the foot large and rather spread as be proper for a water dog well clothe with hair stern -- the stern cover with the shortest of hair except for the first couple of inch next the buttock whiplike or stinglike -lrb- a most important point -rrb- and carry low not like a hound 's coat -- the coat compose entirely of short crisp curl not woolly like a poodle 's and very dense if leave to itself this coat mat or cord but this be not permissible in show dog the hair on the muzzle and forehead below the topknot be quite short and smooth as well as that on the stern general appearance -- be not remarkable for symmetry but be quaint and intelligent look height -- the height should be between 21 and 23 inch \* \* hair below that point the hock should be short and wide apart tail -- should be dock from five to seven inch set low and not carry above the level of the back thickly clothe with moderately long feather coat -- body coat abundant flat or slightly wave with no tendency to curl moderately well feathered on leg and stern but clean below the hock color -- rich golden liver this be a certain sign of the purity of the breed dark liver or puce denote unmistakably a recent cross with the black or other variety of field spaniel general appearance -- rather massive and muscular but with free movement and nice tail action denote a tractable and cheerful disposition weight from 35 lb to 45 lb \* \* \* \* \* vi the field spaniel -- the modern field spaniel may be divide into two class indeed combine with tan the spaniel club furnish the follow description of the black field spaniel : -- \* \* \* \* \* head -- should be quite characteristic of this grand sport dog as that of the bloodhound feather below the hock objectionable coat -- flat or slightly wave and never curl sufficiently dense to resist the weather and not too short silky in texture glossy and refine in nature with neither tail and hind-quarter should be similarly adorn color -- jet black throughout glossy and true a little white on chest though a drawback not a disqualification general appearance -- that of a sport dog capable of learn and do anything possible for he inch and conformation a grand combination of beauty and utility \* \* \* \* \* vii the english springer -- it be only quite recently that the kennel broad with a stop and well-developed temple jaw -- long and broad not snipy with plenty of thin lip eye -- medium size not too full but bright and intelligent of a rich brown ear -- of fair length low girth and chest deep and fairly broad loin -- rather long strong and slightly arched hind-quarter and hind-leg -- very muscular hock well let down stifle moderately bent and not twist inwards or outwards foot -- strong and compact stern -- low carry not above the level of the back and with a vibratory motion coat -- thick and smooth or very slightly wavy it must not be too long the feather must be only moderate on the ear and scanty on the leg but continue down to the heel color -- liver and white and black and white -lrb- with or without tan -rrb- fawn and white yellow and white also roan and self color of all these tint the pied color be preferable however as more easily see in cover general appearance -- a active compact dog upstand but by no means stilty he height at shoulder should about equal he length from the top of the withers to the root of the tail \* \* \* \* \* viii the welsh springer -- like the english springer the welsh springer have only very recently come for endurance and activity and about 28 lb and upward in weight but not exceed 45 lb \* \* \* \* \* ix the cocker spaniel -- for the last few year the popularity of this smaller size branch of the compare very favourably with we own the descriptive particulars of the breed be : -- \* \* \* \* \* head -- not so heavy in proportion and not so high in occiput as in the modern field spaniel with a nicely develop muzzle or jaw lean but not snipy and yet not so square as in the clumber or sussex variety but always exhibit a sufficiently wide and well-developed nose forehead perfectly smooth rise without a too decide stop from muzzle into a comparatively wide and round well-developed skull with plenty of room for brain power eye -- full but not prominent hazel or brown color with a general expression of intelligence and gentleness though decidedly wideawake bright and merry never goggle nor weak as in the king charle and blenheim kind ear -- lobular set on low leather fine and not exceed beyond the nose well clothe with long silky hair which must be straight or wavy -- no positive curl or ringlet neck -- strong and muscular and neatly set on to fine sloping shoulder body -lrb- include size and symmetry -rrb- -- not quite so long and low as in the other breed of spaniel more compact and firmly knit together give the impression of a concentration of power and untiring activity weight -- the weight of a cocker spaniel of either sex should not exceed 25 lb or be less than 20 lb any variation either way should be penalize nose -- sufficiently wide and well develop to ensure the exquisite scent power of this breed shoulder and chest -- the former sloping and fine chest deep and well develop but not too wide and round to interfere with the free action of the fore-leg back and loin -- immensely strong and compact in proportion to the size and weight of the dog slightly slope towards the tail hind-quarter -- wide well round and very muscular so as to ensure untiring action and propel power under the most try circumstance of a long day bad weather rough ground and dense covert stern -- that most characteristic of blue blood in all the spaniel family may in the lighter and more active cocker although set low down be allow a slightly higher carriage than in the other breed but never cock up over but rather in a line with the back though the lower its carriage and action the better and when at work its action should be incessant in this the brightest and merriest of the whole spaniel family foot and leg -- the leg should be well bone feathered and straight for the tremendous exertion expect from this grand little sport dog and should be sufficiently short for concentrated power but not too short as to interfere with its full activity foot firm round and cat-like not too large spreading and loose joint this distinct breed of spaniel do not follow exactly on the line of the larger field spaniel either in lengthiness lowness or otherwise but be shorter in the back and rather higher on the leg coat -- flat or wave and silky in texture never wiry woolly or curly with sufficient feather of the right sort viz wave or setter-like but not too profuse and never curly general appearance -- confirmatory of all indicate above viz a concentration of pure blood and type sagacity docility good temper affection and activity chapter xxvi the basset-hound the basset be not familiarly know to british sportsman before 1863 in which year specimen of the breed be see at the first exhibition of dog hold in pari and cause general curiosity and frequently be adapt with some success they note be resonant with wonderful power for so small a dog and in tone it resemble the voice of the bloodhound the basset-hound be usually very good temper and he companion in the pack when he be most painstaking and indefatigable endowed with remarkable power of scent he will hunt a drag with keen intelligence there be now several pack of basset keep in england and they show very fair sport after the hare but it be not they natural vocation and they massive build be against the possibility of they become popular as harrier the general custom be to follow they on foot although occasionally some sportsman use pony they pace however hardly warrant the latter expedient on the continent where big game be more common than with we the employment of the basset be vary he be a valuable help in the tracking of boar wolf and deer and he be also frequently engage in the lighter pastime of pheasant and partridge shooting the earl of onslow and the with the sport property of this long-bodied breed be apt to refer smilingly to the dachshund as the dog that be sell by the yard and few even of those who know he give credit to the debonair little fellow for the grim work which he be intend to perform in do battle with the vicious badger in its lair dachshund mean badger dog and it be a title fairly and squarely earn in he native germany give proper training he will perform the duty of several sport breed roll into one possess a wonderful nose combine with remarkable steadiness he kind will work out the coldest scent and once fairly on the line they will give plenty of music and get over the ground at a pace almost incredible dachshund hunt well in a pack and though it be not they recognize vocation they can be successfully use on hare on fox and any form of vermin that wear a furry coat but he legitimate work be direct against the badger in locate the brock under ground worry and drive he into he innermost earth and there hold he until dig out it be no part of he call to come to close grip though that often happen in the confine space in which he have to work in this position a badger with he powerful claw dig with such energy and skill as rapidly to bury himself and the dachshund need to be provide with such apparatus as will permit he to clear he way and keep in touch with he formidable quarry the badger be also hunt by dachshund above ground usually in the mountainous part of germany and in the grow crop of maize on the lower slope where the vermin work terrible havoc in the evening in this case the badger be round up and drive by the dog up to the gun which be post between the game and they earth for this sport the dog use be heavier coarser and of larger build higher on the leg and more generally houndy in appearance dachshund be frequently use for deer drive in which operation they be especially valuable as they work slowly and do not frighten or overrun they quarry and can penetrate the densest undergrowth pack of dachshund may sometimes be engage on wild boar and as they be web-footed and excellent swimmer there be no doubt that they terrier quality would make they useful assistant to the otterhound apropo of they capability in the water it be the case that a year or two ago at offenbach-on-main at some trial arrange for life-saving by dog a dachshund carry off the first prize against all comer as a companion in the house the dachshund have perhaps no compeer he be a perfect gentleman cleanly in he habit obedient unobtrusive incapable of smallness affectionate very sensitive to rebuke or to unkindness and amusingly jealous as a watch he be excellent quick to detect a strange footstep valiant to defend the threshold and to challenge with deep voice any intruder yet sensibly discerning he master 's friend and not annoy they with prolonged growling and grumble as many terrier do when a stranger be admit properly bring up he be a perfectly safe and amusing companion for child full of animal spirit and ever ready to share in a romp even though it be accompany by rough and tumble play in germany where he be the most popular of all dog large or small he be to be find in every home from the emperor 's palace downward and he quaint appearance couple with he entertaining personality be daily seize upon by the comic papers to illustrate countless joke at he expense the origin of the dachshund be not very clear some writer have profess to trace the breed or representation of it on the monument of the egyptian some aver that it be a direct descendant of the french basset-hound and other that he be related to the old turnspit -- the dog so excellent in kitchen service of whom dr caius write that when any meat be to be roasted they go into a wheel where they turn about with the weight of they body so diligently look to they business that no drudge nor scullion can do the feat more cunningly whom the popular sort hereupon term turnspit certainly the dog commonly use in this occupation be long of body and short of leg very much resemble the dachshund in all probability the dachshund be a manufactured breed -- a breed evolve from a large type of hound intermix with a terrier to suit the special condition involve in the pursuit and extermination of a quarry that unchecked be capable of seriously interfere with the cultivation of the land he comprise in he small person the characteristic of both hound and terrier -- he wonderful power of scent he long pendulous ear and for he size enormous bone speak of he descent from the hound that hunt by scent in many respects he favor the bloodhound and one may often see dachshund which have be breed from parent carefully select to accentuate some fancy point have exhibit the very pronounced peak -lrb- occipital bone -rrb- the protrude haw of the eye the loose dewlap and the color marking characteristic of the bloodhound he small stature iron heart and willingness to enter the earth bespeak the terrier cross the dachshund be first introduce to this country in sufficient number to merit notice in the early ` sixty and speedily attract notice by he quaint formation and undoubted sport instinct soon become a favorite at first appear at show in the foreign dog class he quickly receive a recognition of he claim to more favored treatment and be promote by the kennel club to a special classification as a sport dog since then he rise have be rapid and he now be reckon as one of the numerically largest breed exhibit unfortunately however he have be little if ever use for sport in the sense that apply in germany and this fact couple with year of breed from too small a stock -lrb- or stock too nearly related -rrb- and the insane strive after the fanciful and exaggerated point demand by judge at dog show many of whom never see a dachshund at he legitimate work have seriously affect he usefulness he have deteriorate in type lose grit and sense too and be often a parody of the true type of dachshund that be to be find in he native land to the reader who contemplate possess one or more dachshund a word of advice may be offer whether you want a dog for sport for show or as a companion endeavor to get a good one -- a well-bred one to arrive at this do not buy from a advertisement on you own knowledge of the breed but seek out a expert amateur breeder and exhibitor and get he advice and assistance if you intend to start a kennel for show purpose do not buy a high-priced dog at a show but start with a well-bred bitch and breed you own puppy under the guidance of the aforementioned expert in this way and by rear and keep you puppy till they be of a age to be exhibit and at the same time carefully note the award at the best show you will speedily learn which to retain and the right type of dog to keep and breed for and in future operation you will be able to discard inferior puppy at a earlier age but it be a great mistake if you intend to form a kennel for show purpose to sell or part with you puppy too early it be notorious with all breed that puppy change very much as they grow the best look in the nest often go wrong later and the ugly duckling turn out the best of the litter this be especially true of dachshund and it require a expert to pick the best puppy of a litter at a month or two old and even he may be at fault unless the puppy be exceptionally well rear to rear dachshund puppy successfully you must not overload they with fat -- give they strengthen food that do not lay on flesh lean raw beef finely chop be a excellent food once or twice a day for the first few month and though this come expensive it pay in the end raw meat be suppose to cause worm trouble but these pest be also find where meat be not give and in any case a puppy be fortify with more strength to withstand they if feed on raw meat than otherwise and a good dosing from time to time will be all that be necessary to keep he well and happy young grow puppy must have they freedom to gambol about and get they leg strong never keep the puppy coop up in a small kennel run or house if you have a fair-sized yard give they the run of that or even the garden in spite of what you gardener may say -- they may do a little damage to the flower but will assuredly do good to themselves they love to dig in the soft border : digging be second nature to they and be of great importance in they development if you have not a garden or if the flower be too sacred it be better to place you puppy as early as possible with respectable cottager or small farmer especially the latter with whom they will have entire freedom to run about and will not be overf if you intend to show you puppy you should begin some time in advance to school they to walk on the lead and to stand quiet when order to much depend on this in the judge ring where a dog who be unused to be on a lead often spoil he chance of appear at he best under the -lrb- to he -rrb- strange experience of restraint which the lead entail during the past five-and-twenty year the name of two particular dachshund stand out head and shoulder above those of they competitor : champion jackdaw standard of point embody a detailed description of the breed : -- \* \* \* \* \* general appearance and disposition -- in general appearance the dachshund be a very long and low dog with compact and well-muscled body rest on short slightly crooked fore-leg a long head and ear with bold and defiant carriage and intelligent expression in disposition the dachshund be full of spirit defiant when attack aggressive even to foolhardiness when attack in play amusing and untiring by nature wilful and unheeding head -- long and appear conical from above and from a side view taper to the point of the muzzle wedge-shape the skull should be broad rather than narrow to allow plenty of brain room slightly arched and fairly straight without a stop but not deep or snipy eye -- medium in size oval and set obliquely with very clear sharp expression and of a dark color except in the case of the liver and tan when the eye may be yellow and in the dapple when the eye may be light or wall-eyed nose -- preferably deep black the flesh-coloured and spotted nose be allowable only in the liver and tan and dapple variety ear -- set on moderately high or see in profile above the level of the eye well back flat not fold pointed or narrow hanging close to the cheek very mobile and when at attention carry with the back of the ear upward and outward neck -- moderately long with slightly arched nape muscular and clean show no dewlap and carry well up and forward fore-quarter -- he work underground demand strength and compactness and therefore the chest and shoulder region should be deep long and wide the shoulder blade should be long and set on very slope the upper arm of equal length with and at right angle to the shoulder blade strong-boned and well-muscled and lie close to rib but move freely the lower arm be slightly bent inwards and the foot should be turn slightly outwards give a appearance of crooked leg approximate to the cabriole of a chippendale chair straight narrow short shoulder be always accompany by straight short upper arm form a obtuse angle badly develop brisket and keel or chicken breast and the upper arm be throw forward by the weight of the body behind cause the leg to knuckle over at the knee broad sloping shoulder on the other hand insure soundness of the fore-leg and foot leg and foot -- fore-leg very short and strong in bone slightly bent inwards see in profile moderately straight and never bend forward or knuckle over foot large round and strong with thick pad compact and well-arched toe nail strong and black the dog must stand equally on all part of the foot body -- should be long and muscular the chest very oval rather than very narrow and deep to allow ample room for heart and lung hang low between front leg the brisket point should be high and very prominent the rib well spring out towards the loin -lrb- not flat-sided -rrb- loin short and strong the line of back only slightly depressed behind shoulder and only slightly arch over loin the hind-quarter should not be higher than the shoulder thus give a general appearance of levelness hind-quarter -- the rump round broad and powerfully muscle hip bone not too short but broad and slope the upper arm or thigh thick of good length and joint at right angle to the hip bone the lower leg -lrb- or second thigh -rrb- be compare with other animal short and be set on at right angle to the upper thigh and be very firmly muscle the hind-leg be lighter in bone than the front one but very strongly muscle with well-rounded-out buttock and the knee joint well develop see from behind the leg should be wide apart and straight and not cowhock the dog should not be higher at the quarter than at shoulder stern -- set on fairly high strong at root and taper but not too long neither too much curved nor carry too high well but not too much feathered a bushy tail be better than too little hair coat and skin -- hair short and close as possible glossy and smooth but resistant to the touch if stroke the wrong way the skin tough and elastic but fitting close to the body color -- _ one color _ : -- there be several self-colours recognize include deep red yellowish red smutty red of these the dark or cherry red be preferable and in this color light shading on any part of the body or head be undesirable black be rare and be only a sport from black and tan _ two color _ : -- deep black brown -lrb- liver -rrb- or gray with golden or tan marking -lrb- spot -rrb- over the eye at the side of the jaw and lip inner rim of ear the breast inside and back of leg the foot and under the tail for about one-third of its length in the above-mentioned color white marking be objectionable the utmost that be allow be a small spot or a few hair on the chest _ dappled _ : -- a silver gray to almost white foundation color with dark irregular spot -lrb- small for preference -rrb- of dark gray brown tan or black the general appearance should be a bright indefinite coloration which be consider especially useful in a hunting dog weight -- dachshund in germany be classify by weight as follow : -- _ light-weight _ -- dog up to 16-1\/2 lb bitch up to 15-1\/2 lb _ middle-weight _ -- dog up to 22 lb bitch up to 22 lb _ heavy-weight _ -- over 22 lb _ toy _ -- up to 12 lb the german pound be one-tenth more than the english the light-weight dog be most use for go to ground chapter xxviii the old working terrier there can hardly have be a time since the period of the norman conquest when the small earth dog which we now call terrier be not know in these island and use by sport man as for terrier dame juliana berner in the fifteenth century do not neglect to include the teroure in she catalogue of sport dog and a hundred year later dr caius give pointed recognition to they value in as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* general appearance -- a terrier calculate to take he own part in the rat pit and not of the whippet type head -- the head should be long flat and narrow level and wedge-shaped without show cheek muscle well fill up under the eye with taper tightly-lipped jaw and level tooth eye -- the eye should be very small sparkling and bright set fairly close together and oblong in shape nose -- black ear -- the correct carriage of ear be a debatable point since crop have be abolish probably in the large breed the drop ear be correct but for toy either erect or semi-erect carriage of the ear be most desirable neck and shoulder -- the neck should be fairly long and taper from the shoulder to the head with sloping shoulder the neck be free from throatiness and slightly arch at the occiput chest -- the chest should be narrow but deep body -- the body should be moderately short and curving upward at the loin rib well spring back slightly arch at the loin and fall again at the join of the tail to the same height as the shoulder foot -- the foot should be more inclined to be cat - than hare-footed tail -- the tail should be of moderate length and set on where the arch of the back end thick where it join the body taper to a point and not carry higher than the back coat -- the coat should be close smooth short and glossy color -- the coat should be jet black and rich mahogany tan distribute over the body as follow : on the head the muzzle be tan to the nose which with the nasal bone be jet black there be also a bright spot on each cheek and above each eye the underjaw and throat be tan and the hair inside the ear be the same color the fore-leg tan up to the knee with black line -lrb- pencil mark -rrb- up each toe and a black mark -lrb- thumb mark -rrb- above the foot inside the hind-legs tan but divide with black at the hock joint and under the tail also tan and so be the vent but only sufficiently to be easily cover by the tail also slightly tan on each side of the chest tan outside the hind-leg -- commonly call breeching -- be a serious defect in all case the black should not run into the tan nor _ vice versa _ but the division between the two color should be well define weight -- for toy not exceed 7 lb for the large breed from 10 to 20 lb be most desirable chapter xxxi the bull-terrier the bull-terrier be now a gentlemanly and respectably own dog wear a immaculate white coat and a burnish silver collar he have dealings with aristocracy and be no longer contemn for keep bad company but a generation or two ago he be sufficiently modern to leave no doubt as to its derivation in the first quarter of the nineteenth century attention be be direct to the improvement of terrier generally and new type be seek for they be alert agile little dog excellent for work in the country but the extravagant corinthian of the time -- the young gamester who patronise the prize-ring and the cock-pit -- desire to have a dog who english white terrier but probably both be use indifferently and for a considerable period the result give the young buck what they require : a dog that be at once a determine vermin killer and a immediate purpose and be highly value for he pertinacity if not for he appearance in 1806 lord camelford possess one for which he have pay the very high price of eighty-four guinea and which he or so ago white be become frequent and be much admire a strain of pure white be breed by jame hink a well-known dog-dealer of birmingham and it be no doubt to hink that we be indebted for the elegant bull-terrier of the type that we know to-day these birmingham dog show a refinement and grace and a absence of the crook-leg and color patch which betray that hink have be use a out-cross with the english white terrier thus get away further still from the bulldog with the advent of the hink strain in 1862 the short-faced dog fall into disrepute and pure white become the accept color there be a wide latitude in the matter of weight if all other point be good a dog might weigh anything between 10 and 38 lb but class be usually divide for those above and those below 16 lb the type become fix deep brisket powerful loin long body a tail set and carry low a fine coat and small ear well hang and drop forward idstone who write this description in 1872 earnestly insist that the ear of all dog cause to fear a further decline in popularity for a variety so eminently engage the club description be as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* general appearance -- the general appearance of the bull-terrier be that of a symmetrical animal the embodiment of agility grace elegance and determination head -- the head should be long flat and wide between the ear taper to the nose without cheek muscle there should be a slight indentation down the face without a stop between the eye the jaw should be long and very powerful with a large black nose and open nostril eye small and very black almond shape prefer the lip should meet as tightly as possible without a fold the tooth should be regular in shape and should meet exactly any deviation such as pigjaw or be underhung be a great fault ear -- the ear when crop should be do scientifically and accord to fashion crop dog can not win a prize at show hold under kennel club rule if bear after march 31st 1895 when not crop it should be a semi-erect ear but other do not disqualify neck -- the neck should be long and slightly arched nicely set into the shoulder taper to the head without any loose skin as find in the bulldog shoulder -- the shoulder should be strong muscular and slant the chest wide and deep with rib well round back -- the back short and muscular but not out of proportion to the general contour of the animal leg -- the fore-leg should be perfectly straight with well-developed muscle not out at shoulder but set on the racing line and very strong at the pastern joint the hind-leg be long and in proportion to the fore-leg muscular with good strong straight hock well let down near the ground foot -- the foot more resemble those of a cat than a hare color -- should be white coat -- short close and stiff to the touch with a fine gloss tail -- short in proportion to the size of the dog set on very low down thick where it join the body and taper to a fine point it should be carry at a angle of about 45 degree without curl and never over the back height at shoulder -- from 12 to 18 inch weight -- from 15 lb to 50 lb chapter xxxii the smooth fox-terrier to attempt to set forth the origin of the fox-terrier as we know he to-day would be of no interest to the general reader and would entail the task of trace back the several heterogeneous source from which he spring it be a matter of very little moment whether he owe he origin to the white english terrier or to the bull-terrier cross with the black and tan or whether he have a mixture of beagle blood in he composition so it will suffice to take he as he emerge from the chaos of mongreldom about the middle of the last century rescue in the first instance by the desire of huntsman or master of well-known pack to produce a terrier somewhat in keep with they hound and in the second place to the advent of dog show prior to that time any dog capable from he size conformation and pluck of go to ground and bolt he fox be a fox-terrier be he rough or smooth black brown or white the starting-point of the modern fox-terrier date from about the ` sixty and no pedigree before that be worth consider from three dog then well know -- old jock trap and tartar -- he claim descent and thanks to the fox-terrier club and the great care take in compile they stud-book he can be bring down to to-day of these three dog old jock be undoubtedly more of a terrier than the other it be a moot point whether he be breed as state in most record of the time by captain percy william master of the rufford or by jack morgan huntsman to the grove it seem however well establish that the former own he sire also call jock and that he dam grove pepper be the property of morgan he first come before the public at the birmingham show in 1862 where show by mr wootton of nottingham he win first prize he subsequently change hand several time till he become the property of mr murchison in whose hand he die in the early ` seventy he be exhibit for the last time at the crystal palace in 1870 and though then over ten year old win second to the same owner 's trimmer at he best he be a smart well-balanced terrier with perhaps too much daylight under he and want somewhat in jaw power but he show far less of the bull-terrier type than do he contemporary tartar this dog 's antecedent be very questionable and he breeder be give as mr stevenson of chester most of whose dog be bull-terrier pure and simple save that they have drop ear and short stern be in this respect unlike old trap whose sire be generally suppose to have be a black and tan terrier this dog come from the oakley kennel and he be suppose to have be breed by a miller at leicester however questionable the antecedent of these three terrier may have be they be undoubtedly the progenitor of we present strain and from they arise the kennel that we have to-day mention have be make of mr murchison and to he we owe in a great measure the start in popularity which since the foundation of he large kennel the fox-terrier have enjoy mr murchison 's chief opponent in the early ` seventy be mr gibson of brockenhurst with he dog tyke and old foiler mr luke turner of leicester with he belvoir strain which later give we ch brockenhurst joe ch olive and she son ch spice mr theodore bassett mr allison and a year or so later mr frederick burbidge the messr clarke mr tinne mr franci redmond and mr vicary about this time a tremendous impetus be give to the breed by the formation in 1876 of the fox-terrier club which owe its inception to mr harding cox and a party of enthusiast seat round he dinner table at 36 russell square among whom be messr bassett burbidge doyle allison and redmond the last two name be still member of the club the idea be very warmly welcome a committee form and a scale of point draw up which with but one alteration be in vogue to-day every prominent exhibitor or breeder then and with few exception since have be a member and the club be by far the strongest of all specialist club it will be well to give here the say standard of point \* \* \* \* \* head and ear -- the _ skull _ should be flat and moderately narrow and gradually decrease in width to the eye not much stop should be apparent but there should be more dip in the profile between the forehead and top jaw than be see in the case of a greyhound the _ cheek _ must not be full the _ ear _ should be v-shaped and small of moderate thickness and drop forward close to the cheek not hang by the side of the head like a foxhound 's the _ jaw _ upper and under should be strong and muscular should be of fair punish strength but not so in any way to resemble the greyhound or modern english terrier there should not be much fall away below the eye this part of the head should however be moderately chisel out so as not to go down in a straight line like a wedge the _ nose _ towards which the muzzle must gradually taper should be black the _ eye _ should be dark in color small and rather deep set full of fire life and intelligence as nearly as possible circular in shape the _ tooth _ should be as nearly as possible level _ ie _ the upper tooth on the outside of the lower tooth neck -- should be clean and muscular without throatiness of fair length and gradually widen to the shoulder shoulder and chest -- the _ shoulder _ should be long and sloping well lay back fine at the point and clearly cut at the withers the _ chest _ deep and not broad back and loin -- the _ back _ should be short straight and strong with no appearance of slackness the _ loin _ should be powerful and very slightly arch the fore rib should be moderately arch the back rib deep and the dog should be well rib up hind-quarter -- should be strong and muscular quite free from droop or crouch the thigh long and powerful hock near the ground the dog stand well up on they like a foxhound and not straight in the stifle stern -- should be set on rather high and carry gaily but not over the back or curl it should be of good strength anything approach a pipe-stopper tail be especially objectionable leg and foot -- the _ leg _ view in any direction must be straight show little or no appearance of a ankle in front they should be strong in bone throughout short and straight to pastern both fore and hind leg should be carry straight forward in travel the stifle not turn outwards the elbow should hang perpendicular to the body work free of the side the _ foot _ should be round compact and not large the sole hard and tough the toe moderately arch and turn neither in nor out coat -- should be straight flat smooth hard dense and abundant the belly and under side of the thigh should not be bare as regard color white should predominate brindle red or liver marking be objectionable otherwise this point be of little or no importance symmetry size and character -- the dog must present a general gay lively and active appearance bone and strength in a small compass be essential but this must not be take to mean that a fox-terrier should be cloggy or in any way coarse -- speed and endurance must be look to as well as power and the symmetry of the foxhound take as a model the terrier like the hound must on no account be leggy nor must he be too short in the leg he should stand like a cleverly-made hunter cover a lot of ground yet with a short back as before state he will then attain the highest degree of propel power together with the greatest length of stride that be compatible with the length of he body weight be not a certain criterion of a terrier 's fitness for he work -- general shape size and contour be the main point and if a dog can gallop and stay and follow he fox up a drain it matter little what he weight be to a pound or so though roughly speak it may be say he should not scale over twenty pound in show condition disqualify point : nose -- white cherry or spot to a considerable extent with either of these color ear -- prick tulip or rise mouth -- much overshot or much undershot \* \* \* \* \* in order to give some idea of the extraordinary way in which the fox-terrier take the public taste it will be necessary to hark back and give a _ resume _ of most animal be a fascinating pursuit that of the fox-terrier present many vary delight chapter xxxiii the wire-hair fox-terrier the wire-hair fox-terrier be with the exception of its coat identical with the smooth fox-terrier -- full brother in fact to he the two variety be much interbreed and several litter in consequence include representative of both and not only this but it be quite a frequent occurrence to get a smooth puppy from wire-hair parent although for some generation neither of the parent may have have any smooth cross in they pedigree the north of england and south wale -lrb- to a lesser extent -rrb- have ever be the home of the wire-hair and nearly all the best specimen have come originally from one or the other of those district there be no doubt that there be although the pedigree therefore may not have be quite right the terrier be invariably pure breed in the early day the smooth be not cross with the wire to anything like the extent that it be later and this fact be probably the cause of the salvation of the variety the wire-hair have have more harm do to he by he be injudiciously cross with the smooth than probably by anything else the greatest care must be exercise in the matter of coat before any such cross be effect the smooth that be cross with the wire must have a really hard and not too full coat and as there be very very few smooth now be show with anything like a proper coat for a terrier to possess the very greatest caution be necessary some few year back almost incalculable harm be do to the variety by a considerable amount of cross into a strain of smooth with terribly soft flannelly coat good-looking terrier be produce and therein lay the danger but they coat be as bad as bad could be and though people be at first too prone to for any terrier to possess and it be not a wire-hair terrier 's coat which ought to be a hard crinkly peculiar-looking broken coat on top with a dense undercoat underneath and must never be mistakable for a elongate smooth terrier 's coat which can never at any time be a protection from wind water or dirt and be in reality the reverse the wire-hair have have a great advertisement for better or with the finger and thumb the kennel club regulation for the preparation of dog for exhibition be perfectly clear on this subject and be word most properly they say that a dog shall be disqualify if that this be the general practice in connection with it chapter xxxv the bedlington terrier this gamest of all the terrier have be know as a distinct and thoroughly british breed for over a century anything indeed he pluck be too insistent the standard of point as adopt by the national bedlington terrier and the yorkshire bedlington terrier club be as follow : -- \* \* \* \* \* skull -- narrow but deep and round high at the occiput and cover with a nice silky tuft or topknot muzzle -- long taper sharp and muscular as little stop as possible between the eye so as to form nearly a line from the nose-end along the joint of skull to the occiput the lip close fitting and without fly eye -- should be small and well sink in the head the blues should have a dark eye the blues and tan ditto with amber shades liver and sandy a light brown eye nose -- large well angled blues and blues and tan should have black nose liver and sandy flesh-coloured tooth -- level or pincher-jawed ear -- good-sized foot which be rather long tail -- thick at the root taper to a point slightly feathered on lower side 9 inch to 11 inch long and scimitar shaped neck and shoulder -- neck long deep at base rise well from the shoulder which should be flat body -- long and well-proportioned flat ribbed and deep not wide in chest slightly arch back well rib up with light quarter coat -- hard with close bottom and not lie flat to side color -- dark blue blue and tan liver liver and tan sandy or sandy and tan height -- about 15 inch to 16 inch weight -- dog about 24 pound bitch about 22 pound general appearance -- he be a light-made lathy dog but not shelly \* \* \* \* \* there be a tendency nowadays towards excess of size in the bedlington it be incline to be too long in the body and too leggy which if not check will spoil the type of the breed it be therefore very important that size should be more study by judge than be at present the case the fault refer to be doubtless the result of breed for exceptionally long head which seem to be the craze just now and of course one can not get extra long head without proportionately long body and large size if it be possible to do so then the dog would become a mere caricature as a sport terrier the bedlington hold a position in the first rank he be very fast and enduring and exceedingly pertinacious and be equally at home on land and in water he will work a otter draw a badger or bolt a fox and he have no superior at kill rat and all kind of vermin he have a exceptionally fine nose and make a very useful dog for rough shooting be easily teach to retrieve if he have any fault at all it be that he be of too jealous a disposition which render it almost impossible to work he with other dog as he want all the fun to himself and if he can not get it he will fight for it but by himself he be perfect as a companion he be peculiarly affectionate and faithful and remarkably intelligent he make a capital house-dog be a good guard and be very safe with child bedlington be not dainty feeder as most writer have assert nor be they tender dog if they be keep in good condition and get plenty of exercise they feed as well as any other and be as hard as nail if not pampered they be easy to breed and rear and the bitch make excellent mother if train when young they be very obedient and they tendency to fight can in a great measure be cure when they be puppy but if not check then it can not be do afterwards once they take to fight nothing will keep they from it and instead of be pleasurable companion they become positive nuisance bull-terrier 's but well-fitting show through the hair they black lining nose -- must be black eye -- a dark hazel color small not prominent and full of life fire and intelligence ear -- small and straight forward when travel the stifle not turn outwards the leg free of feather and cover like the head with as hard a texture of coat as body but not so long coat -- hard and wiry free of softness or silkiness not so long as to hide the outline of the body particularly in the hind-quarter straight and flat no shagginess and free of lock or curl color -- should be whole-coloured the most preferable be bright red red wheaten or yellow red white sometimes appear on chest and foot it be more objectionable on the latter than on the chest as a speck of white on chest be frequently to be see in all self-coloured breed size and symmetry -- the most desirable weight in show condition be for a dog 24 lb and for a bitch 22 lb the dog must present a active lively lithe and wiry appearance graceful racing outline temperament -- dog that be very game be usually surly or snappish the irish terrier as a breed be a exception be remarkably good-tempered notably so with mankind it be admit the wire-hair fox-terrier the jaw should be powerful clean cut rather deeper and more punish -- give the head a more masculine appearance -- than that usually see in a fox-terrier the stop not too define fair length from stop to end of nose the latter being of a black color ear -- the ear should be v-shaped small not too thin set on fairly high carry forward and close to the cheek eye -- the scottish terrier the scottish terrier as a show dog date from about 1877 to 1879 he seem almost at once to have attain popularity and he have progress gradually since then ever in a upward direction until he be to-day one of the most popular and extensively own variety of the dog sir paynton pigott have at the date mention a very fine kennel of the breed for in _ the live stock journal _ of may 30th 1879 we find he kennel fully review in a most enthusiastic manner by a correspondent who visit it in consequence of a controversy that be go on at the time as to whether or not there be such a strongly of opinion that there still exist in scotland at the present time specimen of the breed which propagate the lot which be what be call even now the highland terrier a little long-backed short-legged snipy-faced prick or drop-eared mostly sandy and black-coloured terrier game as a pebble lively as a cricket and all in all a most charming little companion and further that to produce we they mr w l mccandlish one of the greatest living authority on the breed in a able treatise publish some time back tell we in reference to this matter that the terrier under notice go at different
